      <li id="BP9">
        <p>Building around Repogrep</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Zuj">
            <p>I’m quite happy with the visuals of Repogrep. This is PP Neue Montreal for headings, Zed Plex Sans for body copy and EK Modena Mono and system monospaces as the monospaced fonts. EK Modena Mono can be thought of as an “accent” mono, since it is not entirely legible at smaller sizes and could be hard to read when using an entire diff for example.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9zdB">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="TTBx">
            <p>I’d like to port the “visual style” of Repogrep over to Ami. This will probably be a somewhat slow integration and will take time, but I think it would be nice. We can make Ami look really first-class with this kind of approach.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="96S7">
        <p>Goodhart’s Law</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="ExYl">
            <p>Goodhart's law is an adage often stated as, "When a measure becomes a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SHYs">
            <p>target, it ceases to be a good measure".[1] It is named after British</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gY">
            <p>economist Charles Goodhart, who is credited with expressing the core</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZS">
            <p>idea of the adage in a 1975 article on monetary policy in the United</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KU6E">
            <p>Kingdom:[2]</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8P">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Uipo">
            <p>https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goodhart%27s_law</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="OE6d">

      <li id="Fa6X">
        <p>Happiness is defined by the bad things that you do not have</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="OL">
            <p>Someone, somewhere, recently wrote something along the lines of:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3v">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lUJo">
            <p>#+begin_quote</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kN">
            <p>Happiness can best be described as the negative, rather than the positive, things that you do not have.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_G8F">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Qb">
            <p>e.g. I am cancer-free.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rR">
            <p>#+end_quote</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QCZx">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="enpJ">
        <p>How floating point numbers work</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="bnEt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qL">
            <p>floating point numbers are a difficult problem for computers. using</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ujj4">
            <p>two's complement, computers can represent both positive and negative</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G7">
            <p>numbers up to some total depending on their word size (number of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6Z">
            <p>bits).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Hcie">
            <p>they use floating point representation to do this.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tWv4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="J5">
            <p>basically they use "to the power of" notation internally. e.g. a number like 3.84 to the power of 10</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pBVY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="X6A8">
            <p>they store 3.84, then they store the "power" value as another data part.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="x5aE">
            <p>you then have 3 main components to consider when storing floating point values:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uG9p">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xUA6">
            <p>1. the sign (is it - or +)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vk">
            <p>2. the main number, e.g. 3.84 (mantissa)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MlsB">
            <p>3. the power, e.g. 10 (exponent part)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DQ">
            <p>floating point numbers are required because they let us have fractions.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uNgE">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="07sf">
        <p/>
        <ul>
          <li id="aKaF">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="blbG">
        <p>File permissions</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="3ksB">
            <p>files have different permissions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2n">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="6x">
            <p>=dired= is pretty helpful for figuring this out. for example in the following dired listing:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xu">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1X">
            <p>#+begin_src</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cVQW">
            <p>-rw-r--r--@   1 benmaclaurin  staff   1428  8 Dec 00:46 20231207T231031--threads-processes-and-concurrency.org</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PR">
            <p>-rw-r--r--@   1 benmaclaurin  staff  76165  8 Dec 01:46 20231208T013803--unix-and-internet-fundamentals-howto.html</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ku">
            <p>-rw-r--r--    1 benmaclaurin  staff  65783  8 Dec 13:05 20231208T013803==1a--unix-and-internet-fundamentals-howto.org</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Sj">
            <p>-rw-r--r--@   1 benmaclaurin  staff    831  8 Dec 13:50 20231208T130628==1b--how-floating-point-numbers-work.org</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r3">
            <p>-rw-r--r--    1 benmaclaurin  staff    825  8 Dec 13:34 20231208T132436==1c--disks.org</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G6">
            <p>-rw-r--r--    1 benmaclaurin  staff    388  8 Dec 13:30 20231208T132614==1d--kernels.org</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DOtd">
            <p>#+end_src</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7M">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="JLO_">
            <p>The permission section is:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8kf5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Kl1">
            <p>#+begin_src</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Csn">
            <p>-rw-r--r--@</p>
          </li>
          <li id="H9y">
            <p>#+end_src</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E_1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="nld">
            <p>which is at the beginning of each file. these are essentially the priviledges</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7eF">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DZ9">
            <p>=-= means a regular file</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8Zs">
            <p>=d= would be directory</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yZA">
            <p>=l= would mean symbolic link</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tdw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_mx">
            <p>** first section is for user priv</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RTC">
            <p>=rw-= means =read= and =write= permissions granted. =-= means no =execute= permission is granted.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p2X">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="AGp">
            <p>essentially this group is the only one worth reading if you are only user on the system</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T3e">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VtT">
            <p>** next section for group priv</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X-8">
            <p>=r--=</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o9Q">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="27t">
            <p>** next section for others</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_Ze">
            <p>=r--=</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RVQ">
            <p>not sure what does the =@= mean?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dV7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="oFN">
            <p>=@= means there are some extended permissions available.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UTm">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7jN">
            <p>you can run =xattr [file]= to view what these permissions are.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SCV_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="m9Ei">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

        <p>Amanda Askell</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="LjbV">
            <p>Head of AI ethics at Claude.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XQ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xo">
            <p>Interesting AI researcher/philosopher</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T4lP">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="a5">
            <p>YouTube (lex fridman): https://youtu.be/ugvHCXCOmm4?feature=shared&amp;t=9773</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_MTw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yK">
            <p>I’m a philosopher working on finetuning and AI alignment at Anthropic. My team</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PpJO">
            <p>trains models to be more honest and to have good character traits, and works on</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ai">
            <p>developing new finetuning techniques so that our interventions can scale to more</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Wz">
            <p>capable models. Before this I worked as a research scientist on the policy team</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vt">
            <p>at OpenAI, where I worked on AI safety via debate and human baselines for AI</p>
          </li>
          <li id="36">
            <p>performance.</p>

          <li id="Fp2x">
            <p/>
          </li>

            <p>I have a PhD in philosophy from NYU with a thesis on infinite ethics and a BPhil</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RO">
            <p>in philosophy from the University of Oxford. I did my undergraduate degree in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ea">
            <p>Philosophy at the University of Dundee, where I started out my academic life as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AewB">
            <p>a fine art and philosophy student at the Duncan of Jordanstone art school. My</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HH">
            <p>philosophy work has mostly revolved around ethics, decision theory, and formal</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hsN3">
            <p>epistemology.</p>

          </li>

      <li id="gL6C">
        <p>Analog cards</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="iiPG">
            <p>I genuinely appreciate the Analog Today cards. They're straightforward</p>
          </li>
          <li id="c7">
            <p>two-sided cards: one side for notes and the other for to-do items. You</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jwKa">
            <p>can indicate an item's completion status by filling in either a half</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ql">
            <p>or full circle. What stands out for me is their intentional simplicity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4S">
            <p>and tangibility. The concept of accumulating a stack of cards</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3X5p">
            <p>throughout the week offers a satisfying approach to note-taking.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-IY1">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="qp23">
        <p>Attractive things work better</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="9XiF">
            <p>Attractive things do work better. Their attractiveness produces positive</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iW">
            <p>emotions, causing mental processes to be more creative, more tolerant of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u2Ab">
            <p>minor difficulties. The three levels of processing lead to three</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uW">
            <p>corresponding forms of design, visceral, behavioural, and reflective.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6X">
            <p>Each plays a critical role in human behaviour, each an equally critical</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uo">
            <p>role in design, marketing, and use of products.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-oyz">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="-JeW">
        <p>Avoid side quests</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="AL3o">
            <p>The founder of Linear talks about avoiding side quests or side quest</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o3">
            <p>lines and having a critical and clear focus on your current</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3N">
            <p>goal. Don't be attracted to shiny distractions.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="yUHq">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="seqa">
        <p>China</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Te">
            <p>The beautiful thing about China is that it really opens the world in a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MV">
            <p>new perspective. You see limitless possibilities and your</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eR">
            <p>understanding of scale truly develops.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qj3j">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="XIQa">
        <p>Before you ask for help</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="t4El">
            <p>- Show that you have skin in the game: When you reach out to an</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HW">
            <p>expert, make them aware of the time, energy, and money you've</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KAWk">
            <p>already invested in the problem. Let them know you've done the work</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PoP4">
            <p>and that you're stuck. When I see requests from someone who shows</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LhA6">
            <p>they're invested in solving a problem, and who demonstrates they've</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8g">
            <p>done their research to craft a pitch around a very specific issue I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Dj">
            <p>can help with, I'm happy and eager to respond. Contrast that with</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xS">
            <p>emails that say, "Hey Shane, what do you think of this investment</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KB8M">
            <p>opportunity?" Which would you be more excited to answer?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jd">
            <p>- Get precise on your ask: Be very clear what you're looking for. Are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G1Hd">
            <p>you looking for them to review your plan and provide feedback? Are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CX">
            <p>you looking for them to introduce you to people who can solve the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4egW">
            <p>problem? Whatever it is that you want, just be clear.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Wu">
            <p>- Show respect for their time and energy: Explicitly stating that the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wM">
            <p>person you're reaching out to is an expert whose time and energy you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="y8">
            <p>respect goes a long way to secure their goodwill. You should also</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aA">
            <p>demonstrate your respect for them, though. For instance, do not ask</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bl">
            <p>for fifteen minutes to pick their brain; instead, ask if they offer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mY">
            <p>one-off consulting sessions and how much they charge for them.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0SPX">
            <p>Experts are expensive and most of the time for good reason. If you're</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0_n-">
            <p>paying $1,000 to $2,000 per hour for some-thing, it forces you to get</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VmUY">
            <p>clear on what you want before you hop on the call. Paying for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0t">
            <p>someone's time not only compensates them for the value they bring to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZkfA">
            <p>the table but forces you to make sure you're not mumbling through the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g9Sr">
            <p>call and wasting their time and yours.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lta-">
            <p>- Ask for their reasons and listen: As mentioned previously, don't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zH">
            <p>just ask experts what they think, ask them how they think. Use them</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ai">
            <p>as a resource to train yourself how to evaluate things so that you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mW">
            <p>can start embodying an expert way of operating. You don't have to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jN">
            <p>agree with what they're saying, but remember: your goal is to learn</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q5">
            <p>from them how to think better, not to have them solve your problem</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p6">
            <p>for you.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7qgK">
            <p>- Follow up: If you want to build a network and make this more than a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wr">
            <p>transactional request, follow up to report on your progress no</p>
          </li>
          <li id="D78b">
            <p>matter what the outcome is. Whether their advice helped you in this</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ry">
            <p>case or not, following up and keeping them updated on your progress</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E0RP">
            <p>primes them</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ksD7">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

        <p>Books and reflections on sanity</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Th">
            <p>I think once you get to a certain /depth of character/, books keep you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="La">
            <p>sane. They keep you sane because you may find comfort in the fact that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6s">
            <p>the author is describing experiences that you yourself have felt and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dZ2C">
            <p>can relate to.</p>

      <li id="WRp">
        <p>It’s easy to find people who agree with you</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="kb68">
            <p>The internet makes it easy to find people who agree with us no matter</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2C">
            <p>what we believe. Want to deny the Holocaust?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NqbG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Jv">
            <p>There's a group for that. Think vaccines cause autism? Many others do</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n_">
            <p>as well. Heck, we still have a flat-earth society, whose membership</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9H">
            <p>spans around the globe.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Lv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="X8">
            <p>You can quickly and easily be surrounded by people who share the same</p>
          </li>
          <li id="15">
            <p>delusions. That doesn't make them true. Reality isn't a popularity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2rzj">
            <p>contest. Surrounding yourself with people who tell you you're right</p>
          </li>
          <li id="44">
            <p>doesn't mean you are.</p>

      <li id="fBOP">
        <p>Elementary physics</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="jUD1">
            <p>** Vectors</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3t">
            <p>Have magnitude, size AND direction.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="om">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="O_">
            <p>** Scalars</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cDck">
            <p>:PROPERTIES:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-N">
            <p>:CUSTOM_ID: h:19E7F2AE-28E1-403F-9BF8-FE048521BFDB</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C0B3">
            <p>:END:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kEYx">
            <p>Have magnitude, size</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DtO8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2mtZ">
            <p>Imagine a brick on the ground.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-PSU">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Txi7">
            <p>A brick can be moved by 5 metres.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hR">
            <p>5 metres is a scalar quantity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sD">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ajkv">
            <p>It can also be considered a distance</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6R">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="md">
            <p>You can specify that a brick moved "5 metres to the right" which includes not only the distance,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ggse">
            <p>but also the direction. This means you have a vector.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wTRk">
            <p>This is also known as displacement. The brick has been displaced 5 metres to the right.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xaO2">
            <p>The change in time is 2 seconds.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="60">
            <p>How fast has it moved if it has moved 5 metres in 2 seconds.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sx">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2-">
            <p>speed = distance/time.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bWb9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="oZ">
            <p>2.5 metres per second.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lN">
            <p>This is a scalar quantity. The speed of the brick is 2.5 metres per second.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i4l8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pv">
            <p>The important thing to remember here is that a scalar is a value without a direction. So when you have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xnc">
            <p>some number alone without a direction, you have a scalar. Otherwise you have a vector.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qId">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5NY">
            <p>So if you just specify some scalar value, without direction, you're giving distance.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vfd">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0ao">
            <p>Else if you are giving both a direction and distance, then you get /displacement/.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bE0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VWd">
            <p>Otherwise if you are talking about speed and direction, then you are taking about velocity.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="en5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5Fc">
            <p>If you don't give direction, you are talking about speed.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wjC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wmH">
            <p>We use S for displacement.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ktf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ILQ">
            <p>Velocity is displacement over time. Speed or rate.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="08R">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="T24">
            <p>Velocity is if you care about your vector direction.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w8c">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="CFr">
            <p>Rate or speed is when you do not care about direction.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n71">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gNc">
            <p>Average velocity because velocity can change over a particular time period.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u93">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dFO">
            <p>5km north / change in time.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nxi">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="h8g">
            <p>A triangle in front of something means the "change in...".</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="4fq4">
        <p/>
      </li>

      <li id="SmX2">
        <p>Energy peaks and troughs</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="PA">
            <p>I think there is this notion of energy peaks and troughs.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="sq">
            <p>I never really used to notice this. Since becoming "present" and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hn">
            <p>"stopping" i am noticing these moments more and more, and I'm able to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Oc">
            <p>seize them.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y27V">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="L9">
            <p>They seem to be these short windows, kind of like bursts. You have to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SIXC">
            <p>be attentitive to them, tuned to their frequency. It's a bit like</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1YQx">
            <p>aircraft, you'll be given a frequency with which you need to tune, but</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n1">
            <p>there is a small window to it. You have to be fast.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vPMf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="uJvp">
            <p>The other thing I'm noticing is that when it comes to hard work, it is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JlWL">
            <p>easy to pamper oneself. Perhaps even worse, it is easy to allow</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kf">
            <p>yourself to be pampered by others. I didn't really suffer through my</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O3">
            <p>degree and work full-time. yeah it was stressful at times, but most of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NB">
            <p>the time i was fine. legit, i had plenty of time to relax, and not</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nH">
            <p>suffer. plenty of time to kick back and relax. i fooled myself into</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Np5o">
            <p>thinking that this was actually a stressful time of my life and when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="L2nB">
            <p>it came up in conversation i would allude to the fact that it did,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ke">
            <p>because it feels great, right. it feels nice to be able to allow</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5p">
            <p>yourself to be told by others that you did something hard. to be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jy">
            <p>recongised. to feel like you are a soldier. but in reality what you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0H_M">
            <p>did was not too difficult and you can actually do it again. in fact,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_h">
            <p>maybe that is only 10% of what you can do.. right? this is only a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yc">
            <p>snapshot of what you can really achieve etc.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JgfH">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vu">
            <p>so, like my father said about an animal, you should not allow yourself</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JF">
            <p>to be pampered, by yourself, or by others....</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="kNtq">
        <p>Fellow Kettle</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="_3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="sB">
            <p>I think the Fellow Kettle is a really good example of where a few</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cm">
            <p>small and bad design choices can ruin the overall product</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DNbN">
            <p>experience. The pouring is unparalleled, so much so that I even use it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TKLA">
            <p>for watering the plants. However, the plastic that covers the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jk">
            <p>instrument on the top of the Fellow is not air-tight, and this means</p>
          </li>
          <li id="peJ5">
            <p>that as the water boils, condensation can accumulate underneath the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7EU3">
            <p>plastic, making it impossible to view the temperature reading. They</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SAAw">
            <p>should have ensured the instrument is clearly visible at all points of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7hA6">
            <p>the boiling process.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yf_N">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="NyAb">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="CW69">
        <p>Boolean algebra</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="a14K">
            <p>interesting concept from the book by charles petzold, second</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QmOI">
            <p>edition. code.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="uO">
            <p>boolean algebra, founded by george boole.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8E">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zrB2">
            <p>this notion of sets. rather than variables with numbers, you have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nmlz">
            <p>variables as classes.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="rB">
            <p>e.g. class C for cat, and have subsets like M for males cats, F for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QI">
            <p>female cats.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4B">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qA7U">
            <p>can then use symbols for unions of classes, etc. so M + F becomes the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u2Jw">
            <p>union of all male and female cats (as sets).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T06b">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-ItP">
            <p>multiplication is used for intersection.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PU">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="WK">
            <p>e.g. if you have B for black cats, W for white, B x F would be all</p>
          </li>
          <li id="og">
            <p>female cats.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Rt">
            <p>kind of acts like a descriptor? "black" and "female"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gr">
            <p>FANTASTIC representation of this on the webside codehiddenlanguages.com</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2MAN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="TrEG">
            <p>[[https://codehiddenlanguage.com/Chapter06/]]</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="YK">
            <p>this has really nice visualisations ; appears to be javascript canvas</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4P">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vj">
            <p>super nice</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tX">
            <p>really helps to understand the notion that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Fh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="YDoo">
            <p>an /intersection/ is AND</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="H8">
            <p>and a /union/ is OR</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="g_">
            <p>switches for an AND gates are in series</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="nIZR">
            <p>switches for an OR gate are in parallel</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qO">
            <p>** telegraphs systems</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8O">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="WnGQ">
            <p>charles talks about telegraph systems. interesting.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Sn">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="CL">
            <p>my first exposure to these was in LOTR films.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="e8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="6k">
            <p>you have mechanical systems.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="HF">
            <p>you also have the burning of haystacks on towers atop mountains as indicators of a battle, etc.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="M9dY">
            <p>these are old forms of relay.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TJp_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Hl">
            <p>morse invents the new version of relay.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="4yBB">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="zTmu">
        <p>Bowie’s best 100 books</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="VB">
            <p>Interviews With Francis Bacon by David Sylvester</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kk">
            <p>Billy Liar by Keith Waterhouse</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3ZG4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="CT">
            <p>Room At The Top by John Braine</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LB">
            <p/>
          </li>

      <li id="nIA7">
        <p>Broken windows</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="bfiZ">
            <p>The Pragmatic Programming Book talks about this notion of broken</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BoeY">
            <p>windows.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zkgC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7hwc">
            <p>I think it applies well to life in general.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="l2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="koQo">
            <p>This notion that once one window is broken, it is likely that a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RPf6">
            <p>building will completely degrade.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gP">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="MA">
            <p>This is the same for habits in general. Once you slip up on one day,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZY">
            <p>it's essentially a broken window. It is likely you will let that habit</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KB">
            <p>completely slip.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jixz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vT">
            <p>#+begin_quote</p>
          </li>
          <li id="c3">
            <p>Don't leave "broken windows" (bad designs, wrong decisions, or poor</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jF">
            <p>code) unrepaired. Fix each one as soon as it is discovered. If there</p>
          </li>
          <li id="76">
            <p>is insufficient time to fix it properly, then board it up.  Perhaps</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oU">
            <p>you can comment out the offending code, or display a "Not implemented"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ToAh">
            <p>message, or substitute dummy data instead. Take some action to prevent</p>
          </li>
          <li id="shFl">
            <p>further damage and to show that you're on top of the situation.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z4Sm">
            <p>#+end_quote</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yqfl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="WJ">
            <p>Just tell yourself "no broken windows".</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BKsw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wQ">
            <p>If you don't like the broken windows analogy you can also always think</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2p">
            <p>about entropy (physics).</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="R1LK">
        <p/>
      </li>

          <li id="eNru">

            <p>https://www.givingwhatwecan.org/</p>

      <li id="ATRT">
        <p>Career terms</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="qu">
            <p>The biggest thing you have to come to terms with in your career is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EDXA">
            <p>this: sure, you'll gain experience. Sure, you can demand a higher</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DB">
            <p>compensation. But you'll always face the same degree of rejection as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Eh">
            <p>when you started, and nothing you do will change that. It hurts,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rj9p">
            <p>because you're left thinking "why? I worked so hard and I'm that much</p>
          </li>
          <li id="USV6">
            <p>more experienced than then", but you've got to remember that the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1C">
            <p>stakes are higher, too.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FreB">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="rh_Y">
        <p>China in 2024</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="GycG">
            <p>In my yearly review of 2023, one word kept coming up. "China". It</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xm">
            <p>appeared in several questions, most notably under "what did you want</p>
          </li>
          <li id="16">
            <p>to do but didn't get the chance?".</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4Guj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="KwND">
            <p>I consider this year to be the year of China. Honestly, as nice as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m5kN">
            <p>Anthony is, my heart just isn't in the U.S. If I manage to save up</p>
          </li>
          <li id="s_">
            <p>enough or run into some great new cash flow, then sure, but my</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-rGy">
            <p>allegiances stay with China for now.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KulD">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="ZJAh">
        <p>Choose optimism</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="9VJq">
            <p>Around the age of twenty-two I realized that my worldview had been</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m9">
            <p>deeply imbued with pessimism and cynicism. It was the culture I grew</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fw">
            <p>up in. A hostility to new ideas, to anything that strays from the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Du">
            <p>norm. An assumption that if things can go wrong, they will go wrong —</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1WEj">
            <p>that malice is pervasive.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fBvH">
            <p>One day, I decided to become an optimist and life became much more</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G-">
            <p>fun.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R-g5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="TF">
            <p>The life of a pessimist is easy but dreary. The life of an optimist is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KPqv">
            <p>hard but exciting. Pessimism is easy because it costs</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3FuC">
            <p>nothing. Optimism is hard because it must be constantly reaffirmed. In</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EW">
            <p>the face of a hostile, cynical world, it takes effort to show that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6_">
            <p>positivity has merit.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ol">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="EK">
            <p>To be an optimist, adopt these assumptions:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="go">
            <p>- The future can be great</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3KFx">
            <p>- People’s intentions are mostly good</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-H">
            <p>- Ideas are fragile and need nurturing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jo">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="M2eg">
            <p>Every new idea is an unrealized dream. Dreams are delicate and easy to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1v">
            <p>destroy. When an idea presents itself, try to imagine the best version</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AS">
            <p>of it — what would make this idea great?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0SUe">
            <p>Pessimism and optimism share a trait: both are self-fulfilling. Your</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uD">
            <p>intention influences the outcome. Call it karma or, simply, effort. I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m6nq">
            <p>would rather inhabit a future that has the possibility of being great.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BN-7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mK">
            <p>Only optimists can create a great future. Only optimists can imagine</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jD">
            <p>it. Only optimists will put in the effort to make it. If you want to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nt">
            <p>create a great future, believe it can happen. Choose optimism.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PKb4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Bm">
            <p>https://stephango.com/optimism</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="rcU1">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="_T5h">
        <p>Chronic victims</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="eS">
            <p>He didn't want me to become a passive person---the kind of person</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7J">
            <p>whose behaviour is dictated by the people and events around him. He</p>
          </li>
          <li id="J7">
            <p>didn't want me to become a chronic victim of circumstances.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0cFD">
            <p>No successful person wants to work with a chronic victim.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pqDM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-K">
            <p>The only people who want to work with victims are other victims.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uyn1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Mhtg">
            <p>If you pay attention to chronic victims, you'll notice how fragile</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4l">
            <p>they are---how dependent their attitudes and feelings are on things</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ug">
            <p>they don't control. When things go their way, they're happy; when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sa">
            <p>things don't, they're defensive, passive-aggressive, and occasionally</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vAMe">
            <p>aggressive-aggressive. If their spouse is in a bad mood, they're in a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yb">
            <p>bad mood too. If they hit traffic on the way to work, they bring their</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nf">
            <p>anger and frustration to work with them. If a project they're leading</p>
          </li>
          <li id="46I0">
            <p>isn't on track, they blame someone on their team.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E8Uv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ix">
            <p>Self-accountability is the strength of realising that even though you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vl">
            <p>don't control everything, you do control how you respond to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZU">
            <p>everything.  It's a mindset that empowers you to act and not just</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z3R0">
            <p>react to whatever life throws at you. It transforms obstacles into</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BA">
            <p>opportunities for learning and growth. It means realising that the way</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Eojg">
            <p>you respond to hardship matters more to your happiness than the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xv">
            <p>hardship itself. And it means understanding that the best path is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hg">
            <p>often just to accept things and move on.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iCbT">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="oHwR">
        <p>ASAP vs ALAP principle</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="TR">
            <p>* The ASAP vs ALAP principle.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FafX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="bFMC">
            <p>Decisions with low consequence and high reversibility you want to make</p>
          </li>
          <li id="px">
            <p>ASAP (as soon as possible).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="On">
            <p>Decisions with high consequence and low reversibility you want to make</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jSlY">
            <p>ALAP (as late as possible).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-pD5">
            <p>E.g.: for decisions in the latter category, you want to spend as much</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nP_2">
            <p>time gathering information as possible. Decisions in the former make</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vR">
            <p>more sense to make quickly because your time is saved in the long run.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3Y">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Oc2U">
            <p>* Before Asking for Help</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q2vN">
            <p>- Show that you have skin in the game: When you reach out to an</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rI">
            <p>expert, make them aware of the time, energy, and money you've</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DT">
            <p>already invested in the problem. Let them know you've done the work</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-Nb8">
            <p>and that you're stuck. When I see requests from someone who shows</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4E">
            <p>they're invested in solving a problem, and who demonstrates they've</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CDU6">
            <p>done their research to craft a pitch around a very specific issue I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f0">
            <p>can help with, I'm happy and eager to respond. Contrast that with</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MI">
            <p>emails that say, "Hey Shane, what do you think of this investment</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eox1">
            <p>opportunity?" Which would you be more excited to answer?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="V0">
            <p>- Get precise on your ask: Be very clear what you're looking for. Are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YS">
            <p>you looking for them to review your plan and provide feedback? Are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P3">
            <p>you looking for them to introduce you to people who can solve the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VE">
            <p>problem? Whatever it is that you want, just be clear.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8A">
            <p>- Show respect for their time and energy: Explicitly stating that the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qywI">
            <p>person you're reaching out to is an expert whose time and energy you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="trum">
            <p>respect goes a long way to secure their goodwill. You should also</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pz">
            <p>demonstrate your respect for them, though. For instance, do not ask</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qzxN">
            <p>for fifteen minutes to pick their brain; instead, ask if they offer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eu">
            <p>one-off consulting sessions and how much they charge for them.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h2">
            <p>- Experts are expensive and most of the time for good rea-son. If</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sb">
            <p>you're paying $1,000 to $2,000 per hour for some-thing, it forces</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WR">
            <p>you to get clear on what you want before you hop on the call. Paying</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hW">
            <p>for someone's time not only compensates them for the value they</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-xFM">
            <p>bring to the table but forces you to make sure you're not mumbling</p>
          </li>
          <li id="78Mx">
            <p>through the call and wasting their time and yours.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u-On">
            <p>- Ask for their reasons and listen: As mentioned previ-ously, don't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OV">
            <p>just ask experts what they think, ask them how they think. Use them</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-X">
            <p>as a resource to train yourself how to evaluate things so that you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CI">
            <p>can start embodying an expert way of operating. You don't have to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hQ">
            <p>agree with what they're saying, but remember: your goal is to learn</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q7">
            <p>from them how to think better, not to have them solve your problem</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xqdk">
            <p>for you.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F4G6">
            <p>- Follow up: If you want to build a network and make this more than a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cTsa">
            <p>transactional request, follow up to report on your progress no</p>
          </li>
          <li id="a0">
            <p>matter what the outcome is. Whether their advice helped you in this</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d3">
            <p>case or not, following up and keeping them updated on your progress</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-t">
            <p>primes them</p>
          </li>
          <li id="03">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="iF6H">
            <p>* Defining Problems</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7b6o">
            <p>** The Definition Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="23OY">
            <p>Take responsibility for defining the problem. Don't let someone define</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d6dR">
            <p>it for you. Do the work to understand it. Don't use jargon to describe</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eQ">
            <p>or explain it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hY">
            <p>** The Root Cause Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="J6">
            <p>Identify the root cause of the problem. Don't be content with simply</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wnUU">
            <p>treating its symptoms.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xO">
            <p>** How to Safeguard the Problem</p>
          </li>
          <li id="v4">
            <p>Build a problem-solution firewall. Separate the problem-defining phase</p>
          </li>
          <li id="91">
            <p>of the decision-making process from the problem-solving phase.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="py">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="HZ">
            <p>** Writing out the problem</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fq">
            <p>Remember that writing out the problem makes the invisible</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZV1D">
            <p>visible. Write down what you think the problem is, and then look at it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="424q">
            <p>then next day. if you find yourself using jargon in your description,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OHmi">
            <p>it's a sign that you don't fully understand the problem. And if you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UmTr">
            <p>don't understand it, you shouldn't be making a decision about it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="acmE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Jn">
            <p>** Use the test of time</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ODVk">
            <p>Test whether you're addressing the root cause of a problem, rather</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XRmE">
            <p>than merely treating a symptom, by asking yourself whether it will</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uiOt">
            <p>stand the test of time. Will this solution fix the problem</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bcg_">
            <p>permanently, or will the problem return in the future? If it seems</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fi">
            <p>like the latter, then chances are you're only treating a symptom.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="scEb">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="b2">
            <p>* Exploring Possible Solutions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f4">
            <p>** The Bad Outcome Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kzf1">
            <p>Don't just imagine the ideal future outcome. Imagine the things that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="N57a">
            <p>could go wrong and how you'll overcome them if they do.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wp2f">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lY">
            <p>** The Second-Level Thinking Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xrww">
            <p>Ask yourself "And then what?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_W">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1B">
            <p>** The 3+ Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gb0G">
            <p>Force yourself to explore at least three possible solutions to a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="72b_">
            <p>problem. If you find yourself considering only two options, force</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dZ">
            <p>yourself to find at least one more.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_o">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Y7">
            <p>** Safeguard</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9WYc">
            <p>Imagine that one of the options is off the table. Take each of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2I">
            <p>options you're considering and one at a time, ask yourself, "What</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Lo">
            <p>would I do if that were not possible?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-v">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="G9">
            <p>** Safeguard</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z5">
            <p>Come up with Both-And options. Try to find ways of combining the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Eg">
            <p>binary. Think not in terms of choosing either X or Y, but rather</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_-">
            <p>having both X and Y.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qS9B">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hT">
            <p>** Opportunity-Cost Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gEkk">
            <p>Consider what opportunities you're forgoing when you choose one option</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bOxB">
            <p>over another.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="8k">
            <p>** The 3-Lens Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HKvQ">
            <p>View opportunity costs through these three lenses:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xqD-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0P34">
            <p>compared with what?  and then what?  at the expense of what?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="417w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VRYc">
            <p>** Tip</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z-Xs">
            <p>if you're having trouble assessing opportunity costs, it sometimes</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2pwn">
            <p>helps to put a price on them. For example, putting a price on those</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mB">
            <p>extra two to three hours a day spent commuting will make them more</p>
          </li>
          <li id="S2X5">
            <p>visible an easier to assess.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ci">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qm">
            <p>* Evaluating options</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hU">
            <p>** The Targeting Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="bv">
            <p>Know what you're looking for before you start sorting through the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jH">
            <p>data.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g0nB">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="GcQ">
            <p>*** The HiFi Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="keB">
            <p>Get high-fidelity information that's close to the source and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xdN">
            <p>unfiltered by other people's biases and interests.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E-O">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="HjS">
            <p>Note to self: historians call this the primary source</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d8A">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VXJ">
            <p>*** Safeguard</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fVl">
            <p>Run an experiment. Try something out to see what kind of results it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wOp">
            <p>yields.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KWg">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jTo">
            <p>*** Safeguard</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XTp">
            <p>Evaluate the motivations and incentives of your sources, remember that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kzt">
            <p>everyone sees things from a limited perspective.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DrJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="eiU">
            <p>*** Safeguard</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oN8">
            <p>When you get information from other people, ask questions that yield</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Lnf">
            <p>detailed answers. Don’t ask people what they think; instead, ask them</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NA9">
            <p>how they think.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PcD">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gb8">
            <p>** When asking people questions about solving a problem:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r6w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jU0">
            <p>Q1: what are the variables you’d use to make this decision if you were</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LBm">
            <p>in my shoes? How do those variables relate to one another?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Pro">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_zo">
            <p>Q2: what do you know about this problem that I (or other people)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oFd">
            <p>don’t? What can you see based on your experience that someone without</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jxa">
            <p>your experience can’t? What do you know that most people miss?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8OX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wN3">
            <p>Q3: what would be your process for deciding if you were in my shoes?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZDf">
            <p>How would you go about doing it? (Or: how would you tell your</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MYe">
            <p>mother/friend to go about doing it?)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YAX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A-e">
            <p>** The HiEx Principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nLN">
            <p>Get high-expertise information, which comes from people with a lot of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F-d">
            <p>knowledge and/or experience in a specific area, and from people with</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kv8">
            <p>knowledge and experience in many areas.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0be">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="j5Y">
            <p>** Safeguard</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7iN">
            <p>Take time to distinguish real experts from imitators. Not everyone who</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5z3">
            <p>claims to be an expert is. Take the time to know the difference.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Fx">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xep">
            <p>* How to differentiate between experts and imitators</p>
          </li>
          <li id="33P">
            <p>- Imitators can't answer questions at a deeper level. Specific</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gfO">
            <p>knowledge is earned, not learned, so imitators don't fully</p>
          </li>
          <li id="L1u">
            <p>understand the ideas they're talking about.* Their knowledge is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="chA">
            <p>shallow. As a result, when you ask about details, or first</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FDx">
            <p>principles or nonstandard cases, they don't have good answers.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ACY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="s5w">
            <p>- Imitators can't adapt their vocabulary. They can explain things</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CSt">
            <p>using only the vocabulary they were taught, which is often full of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ml8">
            <p>jargon. Because they don't fully understand the ideas behind the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vIS">
            <p>vocabulary, they can't adapt the way they talk about those ideas to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QqC">
            <p>express them more clearly to their audience.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jdd">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ri0">
            <p>- Imitators get frustrated when you say you don't under-stand. That</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r6i">
            <p>frustration is a result of being overly concerned with the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HK1">
            <p>appearance of expertise—which they might not be able to maintain if</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EHG">
            <p>they have to really get into the weeds with an explanation. Real</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kfc">
            <p>experts have earned their expertise and are excited about trying to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w3i">
            <p>share what they know.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wuF">
            <p>They aren't frustrated by your lack of understanding; they instead</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pMI">
            <p>love your genuine curiosity about something they care about.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YQq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="I12">
            <p>- Experts can tell you all the ways they've failed. They know and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VTf">
            <p>accept that some form of failure is often part of the learning</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6NF">
            <p>process. Imitators, however, are less likely to own up to mistakes</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d7s">
            <p>because they're afraid it will tarnish the image they're trying to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X0p">
            <p>project.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yR6">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="o_f">
            <p>- Imitators don't know the limits of their expertise. Experts know</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pwc">
            <p>what they know, and also know what they don't know. They understand</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uyb">
            <p>that their understanding has boundaries, and they're able to tell</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ffkm">
            <p>you when they're approaching the limits of their circle of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jKd">
            <p>competence. Imitators can't. They can't tell when they're crossing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fmN">
            <p>the boundary into things they don't understand.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mwz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="x0w">
            <p>* Live with a decision before announcing it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qBK">
            <p>Make major decisions and then sleep on them before telling</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O52">
            <p>anybody. Also before going to bed, write a note to self about why that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uM9">
            <p>decision was made.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nCs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ERa">
            <p>* When you'll know you've hit the limit of useful information</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vp6">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ddz">
            <p>- You are able to argue credibly for and against the options you're</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Uiy">
            <p>considering from all angles.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n6S">
            <p>- You're stretching for insight by asking people for advice who are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TNC">
            <p>more than one step removed from the problem or who don't have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G61">
            <p>experience solving problems of this sort.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xYF">
            <p>- You feel like you need to learn more, but you've stopped learning</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p_v">
            <p>new things, and are instead in a constant loop reviewing the same</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8Y5">
            <p>information (or same arguments) over and over.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kct">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="9m_">
            <p>* Creating a margin of safety</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FZT">
            <p>- The margin of safety is often sufficient when it can absorb double</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Vx">
            <p>the worst-case scenario. So the baseline for a margin of safety is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t4G">
            <p>one that could withstand twice the amount of problems that would</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AsE">
            <p>cause a crisis, or maintain twice the maount of resources needed to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SFS">
            <p>rebuild after a crisis.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xtQ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mYl">
            <p>* Execution fail safes</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GJ3">
            <p>** Set up trip wires to determine in advance what you'll do when you hit a speicifc quantifiable time, amount of circumstance</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dfS">
            <p>** Use commander's intent to empower othes to act and make decisions without you.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CyK">
            <p>*** Who needs to know my goals and the outcomes I'm working toward?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RVG">
            <p>*** Do they know what the most important objective is?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cP3">
            <p>*** Do they know the positive and negative signs to look for and what trip wires are attached to them?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1I4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="56F">
            <p>* Evaluating a particular decision</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2_T">
            <p>When you evaulate a decision, focus on the process you used to make</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ITK">
            <p>the decision and not the outcome.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WaZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Vhv">
            <p>* Transparency principle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sPB">
            <p>Make your decision making process as visible and open to scrutiny as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m1u">
            <p>possible.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LNh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="LM3">
            <p>* Keep a record of your thoughts at the time you make the decision. Don't rely on your memory after the fact. Trying to recall what you knew and thought at the time you made the decision is a fool's game.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jYM9">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="mdEo">
        <p>Clocks in computers</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="sU">
            <p>you'd think clocks store time. whenver i heard about clocks in computers i immediately thought about time.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QmzM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jRlW">
            <p>clocks seem to be used for previous value storage.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Je">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xR">
            <p>they are a bit like a flag. if 1, remember the value set at the time the clock set 1, else remember nay new inputs</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UQ">
            <p>to the gates, etc.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A6F1">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="zApZ">
        <p>Clown attacks</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Vouu">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="WI">
            <p>The core dynamic of clown attacks is that perception of social status</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1UKf">
            <p>affects what thoughts the human brain is and isn't willing to think.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PV">
            <p>This can be used by intelligence agencies and governments to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ky">
            <p>completely deny access to specific lines of thought. Generally,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rSU1">
            <p>there's a lot of ways to socially engineer someone's world model by</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MD">
            <p>taking a target concept and having the wrong people say it at specific</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dpHR">
            <p>times and in specific ways. Clown attacks include having right-wing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BKYL">
            <p>clowns being the main people who are seen talking about the Snowden</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1WDU">
            <p>revelations, or degrowthers being the main people talking about the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h0">
            <p>possibility that technological advancement/human capabilities will end</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1P">
            <p>it's net-positive trend. These are only specific examples of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iQ">
            <p>cost-efficient ways to use a specific circumstance (clowns) to change</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Raj5">
            <p>the way that someone feels about a targeted concept.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TU">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zq">
            <p>With clown attacks, the exploit/zero day is the human tendency to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ge">
            <p>associate specific lines of thought with low social status or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bj">
            <p>low-status people, which will consistently inhibit the human brain</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TJ">
            <p>from pursuing that targeted line of thought.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Wk">
            <p>Although clown attacks may seem mundane on their own, they are a case</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t7LJ">
            <p>study proving that powerful human thought steering technologies have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="U-">
            <p>probably already been invented, deployed, and tested at scale by AI</p>
          </li>
          <li id="upWY">
            <p>companies, and are reasonably likely to end up being weaponised</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7tvL">
            <p>against the entire AI safety community at some point in the next 10</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Wj">
            <p>years.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GM0O">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="pBxl">
        <p>Conservation of energy</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="0EmT">
            <p>It is becoming more clear to me how the principles of physics apply to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EVUp">
            <p>everyday life.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="na">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yY">
            <p>Take for example the conservation of energy. You have some set amount</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_Tux">
            <p>of potential energy which you can transfer into a different type of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r5">
            <p>energy. But you cannot create any new energy. The energy is a constant.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="rCMI">
            <p>For example, when you drop a ball. Before dropping that ball, the ball is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bu7X">
            <p>said to have potential energy. When you drop the ball, that potential energy</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cK">
            <p>is converted into kinetic energy.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pla9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fm">
            <p>I think this quite nicely demonstrates the principle of opportunity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R_0z">
            <p>cost in decision making.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-j">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="RE">
            <p>You have potential to make a decision that takes you in one direction or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p9rr">
            <p>another. If you choose one direction, you are taking your finite energy</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k3">
            <p>and converting it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B4C5">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="vYun">
        <p>Disks</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="OG">
            <p>disks are kind of interesting. they are broken into a number of parts.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oNa1">
            <p>the parts are known as "partitions". different partitions have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WCUn">
            <p>different purposes.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ut6N">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VRF5">
            <p>the lowest number partition usually gets special treatment. it is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mn">
            <p>typically reserved for boot partitioning. it is where you can keep a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QWfk">
            <p>kernel (see notes on kernels 1d).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W50A">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="I5Rv">
            <p>partitions are either swap space (this is used for virtual memory) or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g750">
            <p>file systems used to store files.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VA">
            <p>there is something called fragmentation in disk storage.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="NH">
            <p>basically fragmentation is a scattering effect because files and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MpJe">
            <p>folders etc. change size over time. it is impossible for the computer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AC">
            <p>to get this from one place. why? need to think about this. instead a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yy">
            <p>scaterring approach is used.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uXW5">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="U5Pw">
        <p>Don’t get discouraged</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="oQ">
            <p>#+begin_quote Anthony</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lz">
            <p>Ben,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wO">
            <p>You are busy.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="s3x0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="UE">
            <p>Finding your job of dreams is hard work , keep driving .</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Hz">
            <p>Don't get discouraged, one of the issues is that with employee laws ,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gj">
            <p>the cost of laying off employees off is very high so companies are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oLNG">
            <p>very cautious and want to make sure that you are a cultural fit .</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f4CI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DE">
            <p>Be sure to ask at interviews , “ please describe your Culture ?”</p>
          </li>
          <li id="L1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Nb">
            <p>At exit of interview ask</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uXi8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="4e">
            <p>“ following our brief interview am I a good fit within your culture?”</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wIoK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="AH">
            <p>Also be sure to ask ,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lt">
            <p>“ what are the next steps and timeline “</p>
          </li>
          <li id="guEK">
            <p/>
          </li>

          </li>
