            <p>not ask ,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="olaI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Fk">
            <p>What is the strategy for success going forward ?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="o4">
            <p>What is the current financial position of the Company?</p>
          </li>

        <ul>

            <p>The British education system is not immune to bias. Previously I have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OY">
            <p>heard criticisms of history curriculums in other countries. Japan,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8c">
            <p>China, America come to mind.</p>

            <p>&lt;&lt;&lt; Japan</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6y">
            <p>&lt;&lt;&lt; America</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BtLz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hE">
            <p>Where is the mention of Dresden in the British history curriculum? I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="04">
            <p>studied WWII quite extensively at school. How come I never heard of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kr">

      <li id="yPTm">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="bJVb">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="ES-u">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="nHzY">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="J_EE">
        <p>iMessage splurge about learning</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="2u84">
            <p>I’ve been using design programs as my new way to learn complex</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ie">
            <p>lideas. After experimenting with various methods over the years:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9D">
            <p>Google maps, mind maps, Org mode, handwritten notes, highlighting +</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zw">
            <p>stickies, this method (designing things) and the freedom to move</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-Y">
            <p>things around spatially is the one that seems to work best for me. It</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5zMu">
            <p>appears that when designing things the concepts become clearer, the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xdnC">
            <p>links also become clearer. One fun use of the “animate” tab is that I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m8">
            <p>can quickly connect ideas together.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="M3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xFNw">
            <p>It is also an enjoyable process</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dfDq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="79">
            <p>I find things like Excalidraw and conventional mind map applications</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gd">
            <p>too rigid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jS">
            <p>Even some of the digital whiteboards are too rigid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vc-u">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Oz">
            <p>Nothing seems to beat the design canvas</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="TMKu">
            <p>I think it is just how my brain works best</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="o8">
            <p>Usually everything is monochrome because colour tends to distract</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MzgS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ePh2">
            <p>It seems to me that shape, proximity (gestalts) and typography and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_1fn">
            <p>photography/imagery are what works best</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bz2O">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qI">
            <p>I’ve found the Sketch app to be better than Figma for this as Sketch</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K0g_">
            <p>is native</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ps">
            <p>It seems speed and responsiveness is also important to letting ideas</p>
          </li>
          <li id="z8">
            <p>flow freely</p>
          </li>
          <li id="v0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="B472">
            <p>Figma still best design tool IMO but only for designing, not for this</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sM">
            <p>style of thinking</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zpSu">
            <p>&lt;&lt;&lt; Figma</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="Ga3n">
        <p/>
      </li>

          <li id="2Tg">
            <p>** What valuable life lesson did you learn this year?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ise">
            <p>You have to learn the fundamentals of:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_oC">
            <p>- microeconomics/economics</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F5SR">
            <p>- psychology</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fBY">
            <p>- mathematics</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3Yu">
            <p>- biology</p>
          </li>
          <li id="L44">
            <p>- physics</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uHE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="GJh">
            <p>...and then apply them as a latticework/framework of models in your head. This is how you should all approach problems.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F1O2">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="zqd">
        <p>Just use HTML</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="unE">
            <p>I've gone through a few cycles when it comes to note-taking.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="11c">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="e7">
            <p><span>I started my journey on platforms like Roam Research, Obsidian, RemNote. I have nothing against these platforms, but they always felt like cutting against the grain. After all, note-taking should be frictionless and simple. I once interviewed at a company, and the interviewee said something that left an impression on me. Roughly: "We use </span><em>as few tools</em><span> as possible at this company. We try to make do with what we have and we rarely download new tools or apps". I think this is why a standalone app to manage notes felt wrong to me.</span></p>
          </li>
          <li id="68C">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="C2">
            <p>After some time I transitioned into hardcore text editors. I tried a lot of them. Vim, Emacs, and the various flavours of both (Doom Emacs, Neovim, the list goes on). I had most success with Emacs. I ended up using tools such as Howm (developed by japanese lecturer), Org-mode (of course), and denote, etc. etc.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xWN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zH7">
            <p>The trouble I had is that I still felt friction. So I'm keeping things stupid simple. Just HTML and just a single document. Those are my rules. HTML makes sense to me as a web dev. Markdown is nice, but HTML gives me more freedom to add a little styling. Plus I have more options for marking up my text. </p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="8xc">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="l3e">
        <p><strong>On the Nova editor</strong></p>
        <ul>
          <li id="F4">
            <p>In an effort to use less apps, and only apps that are "mac"-friendly, I'm trying out the Nova editor for everything now. I cannot move off of Cursor easily, because the company has a Cursor team plan. So I'll be using the "agents" view in order to make requests, with GPT-5.2 which I determine to be the best model right now. The current lay of the land is as follows:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aR" data-type="unordered">
            <p>For editor, I can use Nova. This includes for Git operations.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aC" data-type="unordered">
            <p>For browser, I want to use either Safari or Orion. I prefer Orion tabs. Both are native, which is nice, however.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kz" data-type="unordered">
            <p>For terminal, I'll also try to use Nova's terminal.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

I was shocked by my own behaviour and how careless I was, and I regret everything. Travelling with you and camping with you has made such a special memory that I will cherish for so many years. I really want to have more adventures with you. I love you so much and I am so sorry. Please forgive me and the hurt I caused you. I never meant for this to happen and I am so upset with myself that I allowed myself to bring pain to you. I love you.</p>

      <li id="7Ax">
        <p>First Person Singular </p>
        <ul>
          <li id="uz8">
            <p>I am particularly fond of this extract, from the first chapter, which</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UN">
            <p>is aptly titled "Cream":</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TEFV">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="83w">
            <p>&gt; "There's nothing worth getting in this world that you can get easily."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rr">
            <p>&gt; Then, as if starting a new paragraph, he briefly cleared his</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ru">
            <p>&gt; throat. "But, when you put in that much time and effort, if you do</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ar">
            <p>&gt; achieve that difficult thing it becomes the cream of your life."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xsx">
            <p>&gt;   "Cream?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rH">
            <p>&gt;   "In French, they have an expression: creme de la creme.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QSA">
            <p>&gt; Do you know it?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ep">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SM">
            <p>&gt;   "I don't." I said. I knew no French.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JH">
            <p>&gt;   "The cream of the cream. It means the best of the best.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jr">
            <p>&gt; The most important essence of life&amp;#x2013;that's the creme de la creme.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_N">
            <p>&gt; Get it? The rest is just boring and worthless."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NE">
            <p>&gt; Murakami</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="yNp_">
        <p>Berkeley Mono Design Principles</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Y0U-">
            <p>Design philosophy:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pb">
            <p>Emergent over prescribed aesthetics.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W0">
            <p>Expose state and inner workings.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jm">
            <p>Dense, not sparse.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f-">
            <p>Explicit is better than implicit.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xk">
            <p>Regiment functionalism.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ToGH">
            <p>Performance is design.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3osB">
            <p>Verbosity over opaqueness.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Q-">
            <p>Ignore design trends. Timeless and unfashionable.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1u">
            <p>Flat, not hierarchical.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="29yc">
            <p>Diametrically opposite of minimalism. As complex as it needs to be.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LG">
            <p>Driven by specifications and datasheets.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o7">
            <p>Beauty emerges automatically without deliberation.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="a4">
            <p>Do not infantilize users.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dH73">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="y-">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="vTa1">
        <p>Rational egoism</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="cZ">
            <p>The principle that an action can only be deemed rational if it is in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iC">
            <p>one's own interests. This makes it a normative form.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_ymn">
            <p>Normativity states that some societal facets are good, others bad. So,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PY">
            <p>framed in this way, rational egoism would state that acting in one's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bx">
            <p>self interest in a rational fashion is good, and other behaviours</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IX">
            <p>should be considered bad.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P0Th">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="b3eJ">
        <p>New weekly workflow</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="VLWD">
            <p>It makes sense to tinker with my setup only on the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lp">
            <p>weekends. Inveitably I will always want to tinker with things, and if</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xb">
            <p>I can limit this urge to my free time (e.g. weekends only) then this</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-q">
            <p>would be ideal. For example, a browser switch: switching from Arc back</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xL">
            <p>to Firefox. This shouldn't really be done on a weekday, rather is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K8">
            <p>should be completed and done on a weekend.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="cD">
            <p>Likely I will now be able to remove such needs and limit them only to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E_">
            <p>weekends where productivity is not paramount.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XJ7Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="8GJs">
        <p>Narrow minds, Kafka on the Shore</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="TkM_">
            <p>Narrow minds devoid of imagination. Intolerance, theories cut off from</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sk">
            <p>reality, empty terminology, usurped ideals, inflexible systems. Those</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dM">
            <p>are the things that really frighten me. What I absolutely fear and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nHc0">
            <p>loathe. Of course it's important to know what's right and what's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Sy">
            <p>wrong. Individual errors in judgement can usually be corrected. As</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wE">
            <p>long as you have the courage to admit mistakes, things can be turned</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xD">
            <p>around. But intolerant, narrow minds with no imagination are like</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QhC1">
            <p>parasites that transform the host, change form and continue to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zb">
            <p>thrive. They're a lost cause, and I don't want anyone like that coming</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f-t2">
            <p>in here."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4gyL">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="B-xp">
        <p>Common thought experiments</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="QStG">
            <p>&lt;a id="org5148c33"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Et">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vC">
            <p># The Double Standard Test</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="H6">
            <p>Are you judging one person (or group) by a different standard than you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DTOz">
            <p>would use for another person (or group)?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nSMl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7C">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mf">
            <p>&lt;a id="org3d0b923"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yi">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="k1">
            <p># The Outsider Test</p>
          </li>
          <li id="l7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="SHDp">
            <p>How would you evaluate this situation if it wasn't your situation?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ao">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ed">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5y">
            <p>&lt;a id="org5a65240"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pr">
            <p># The Conformity Test</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Pq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="LV">
            <p>If other people no longer held this view, would you still hold it?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MYvK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="QL">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgc63355d"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="B4">
            <p># The Selective Skeptic Test</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Pf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mV">
            <p>If this evidence supported the other side, how credible would you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6D">
            <p>judge it to be?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="EI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ab">
            <p>&lt;a id="org9f7e1bd"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3YHv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xf">
            <p># The status Quo Bias Test</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="21">
            <p>IF your current situation was not the status quo, would you actively</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wH">
            <p>choose it?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VLYh">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="MrsA">

      <li id="WW4H">
        <p>Evergreen Notes</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="fIiM">
            <p>A guy called Andy Matuschak invented a form of note-taking called</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gm">
            <p>"[Evergreen notes](https://notes.andymatuschak.org/About_these_notes)". My understanding is that it involves "atomic notes"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x4">
            <p>and improvements on the [Zettelkasten](https://zettelkasten.de/) system.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yWLN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="cB">
            <p>It is used by [Stephan Ango](https://stephanango.com/), the guy who invented Obsidian.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>

      <li id="PJ2c">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="W_Ot">
        <p>Surround yourself with books</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="IhTu">
            <p>I think it was [Patrick Collison](https://patrickcollison.com/) who said fill common surfaces with</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Iw">
            <p>lots of books. This will keep you reading. It will remind you to read,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sJ">
            <p>and you'll be immersed in an environment where you are reading often.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E9dV">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>

      <li id="b7AM">
        <p>Women are more logical than men</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="-Jx9">
            <p>Here's an interesting thought. I've always found women to be easier to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Uq">
            <p>talk to. This is probably because they are better listeners. I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lq">
            <p>realise, however, there is an element of [ego](20230327T102127--rational-egoism.md) at play. It is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Fq">
            <p>one-sided. When it's their turn to talk, I'm characteristically male,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mC">
            <p>I often don't listen.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ui">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dp">
            <p>It is a stereotype that women only know feelings and men logic. But as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yF">
            <p>Noah Yuval Harari very aptly puts, feelings are evolutionary</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oFRe">
            <p>[logic](20221218T162245--bills-response-to-anticipating-parallel-self.md). Evolutionary logic that may be misplaced in today's society</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GR">
            <p>when confronted with certain problems of a modern archetype, but</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1o">
            <p>still, they are evolutionary. I never considered feelings in this way</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kS">
            <p>before. This would characterise male "logic" as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_q7C">
            <p>machine-like. Superficial. Clinical. Unfeeling. Are women better</p>
          </li>
          <li id="j-">
            <p>"humanes"?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7qqP">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>

        <p>New favourite place to think and write</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="ek">
            <p>22 GF Northumberland Street.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vway">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kv">
            <p>Sitting in the kitchen, I can look out the window at night. There is a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oO">
            <p>green streetlight. It is very comforting, as if time has stopped. You</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IA">
            <p>can see it from the bedroom, but I do not wish to lie down.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="e0">
            <p/>

            <p>My only problem is that the wifi is limited here. But is that a</p>
          </li>

            <p>problem? Maybe what I need is no wifi. An ability to disconnect. To</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xGC">
            <p>"re-charge". If I can setup tasks whilst I have a connection, I can</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dt8">
            <p>continue them here.</p>

          </li>

          </li>

      <li id="ZmLO">
        <p>Steph Ango on writing todos</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="MbMb">
            <p>I've just tried GTD. I don't like it. It doesn't work. For some reason</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2e">
            <p>my stuff is not synchronised. It pissed me off.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4lGI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Sz">
            <p>I sort of like [Stephan Ango's approach here](https://stephanango.com/todos). Make a list weekly of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ha">
            <p>important things to do. The rest will fall away naturally. You can</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7c">
            <p>sort the signal from the noise this way.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pJ">
            <p>Any "habits" should be ingrained to the extent that you don't need to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ld">
            <p>write them out.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bdYm">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="gHwC">
        <p>Jonathan Blow on time management</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="jvZl">
            <p>Basically: "[you don't need time management](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3SW7CsUrIy4)".</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KL">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gg">
            <p>What you want to do is track the time spent *doing the thing*.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ft">
            <p>This is the real metric. Don't plan you time -&gt; ass in chair</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uq">
            <p>mindset. This roughly maps to [Stephan Ango's practice of weekly to-do</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sS">
            <p>lists](20230716T140306--stephen-ango-on-writing-to-dos.md).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mq61">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="YrSX">
        <p>Jonathan Blow on burnout and productivity</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="wf-J">
            <p>Interesting talk on burnout, productivity and ambition. [Watch on</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fz">
            <p>YouTube here](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zewGodTzZ2Y). It is important to be [mindful about where and when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vV">
            <p>productivity is important](20230702T162402--new-workflow-weekly.md).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZQ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hA">
            <p>This relates to his other talk on [getting things done and time management](20230716T140526--jonathan-blow-on-time-management.md).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xGX_">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="h2yd">
        <p>Storing Emacs configuration on iCloud Drive</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Pc1K">
            <p>Sure, to store your Emacs configuration file (typically a file named</p>
          </li>
          <li id="L8">
            <p>".emacs" or a directory named ".emacs.d") on your iCloud Drive and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="czZC">
            <p>make Emacs use that configuration, you can follow the steps below:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WJZ4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dfis">
            <p>1.  ****Backup your existing Emacs configuration****: Before making any</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="SR">
                <p>changes, make sure to backup your existing Emacs configuration</p>
              </li>
              <li id="pQ">
                <p>files. They are typically located in your home directory \`~\`. The</p>
              </li>
              <li id="dJ">
                <p>primary configuration file is usually named \`.emacs\`, and some</p>
              </li>
              <li id="6z">
                <p>configurations are stored in a directory named \`.emacs.d\`.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="an">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="hs">
            <p>2.  ****Move your Emacs configuration to iCloud Drive****: iCloud Drive on</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="xy">
                <p>macOS is typically found at \`~/Library/Mobile</p>
              </li>
              <li id="UB">
                <p>Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs\`. Move your Emacs configuration file</p>
              </li>
              <li id="xC">
                <p>or directory into this directory. If you're using Terminal, you can</p>
              </li>
              <li id="rA">
                <p>use the \`mv\` command to do this. For example:</p>
              </li>
              <li id="MH">
                <p/>
                <ul>
                  <li id="uj">
                    <p>mv ~/.emacs.d ~/Library/Mobile\ Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/</p>
                  </li>
                  <li id="LO">
                    <p/>
                  </li>
                </ul>
              </li>
              <li id="oD">
                <p>This moves your Emacs configuration to your iCloud Drive.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Fs">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="-M">
            <p>3.  ****Create symbolic links to the new location****: Emacs will still</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="KW">
                <p>look for your configuration in your home directory, so you need to</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Ja">
                <p>create symbolic links from the original location to the new</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Mg">
                <p>location. You can use the \`ln -s\` command in Terminal to create</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Fp">
                <p>these symbolic links. For example:</p>
              </li>
              <li id="YG">
                <p/>
                <ul>
                  <li id="Z7">
                    <p>ln -s ~/Library/Mobile\ Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/.emacs.d ~/.emacs.d</p>
                  </li>
                  <li id="oX">
                    <p/>
                  </li>
                </ul>
              </li>
              <li id="v9">
                <p>This creates symbolic links from your home directory to your Emacs</p>
              </li>
              <li id="sT">
                <p>configuration on iCloud Drive.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="OF">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="FF">
            <p>4.  ****Check your setup****: Open Emacs to check that your configuration</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="6H">
                <p>is working correctly. If Emacs opens with your settings, the setup</p>
              </li>
              <li id="bA">
                <p>is successful.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Mkpq">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="dP">
            <p>Remember that changes to files in iCloud Drive are uploaded to iCloud,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q4tp">
            <p>so you'll need an internet connection for changes to sync. If you make</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DS">
            <p>changes to your Emacs configuration while offline, the changes won't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QQ">
            <p>sync to iCloud until you're online again.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kx">
            <p>As of my last training data in September 2021, Apple doesn't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Uj">
            <p>officially support app-specific files (like \`.emacs\` or \`.emacs.d\`) in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1U">
            <p>iCloud Drive across multiple macOS devices, so your mileage may vary</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jC">
            <p>depending on how iCloud Drive is implemented on your specific devices</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0o11">
            <p>and software versions.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OckJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="ZMI2">
        <p>Understanding bidding and timing systems</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="gh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="MC">

          <li id="IELW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Zi_S">
            <p># University Study</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Dm">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tt">
            <p>Practicals 5, 6 and 7 and Lectures 6 and 7 for inspiration</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="4o">
            <p>The three dimensions of auction protocols</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5B">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kT">
            <p>1.  What price does the winner pay (e.g. highest or second highest bid)?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6d">
            <p>2.  Are the bids of agents known to each other (open cry or sealed bid)?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aF">
            <p>3.  How does bidding proceed (singe-shot, repeated ascending, or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9G">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Kb">
            <p>repeated descending)?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zF">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="nED">
            <p>Proposal of a single-unit and multi-unit energy auction framework for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="My2">
            <p>P2P transactions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9Uf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mXe">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ul_">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgbc69441"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2kl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ee1">
            <p>## Prosumers</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JRj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="k-p">
            <p>Consume and provide. Bi-directional transactions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7wA">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DM5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DOQ">
            <p>&lt;a id="org2d8e8c4"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-wK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jOG">
            <p>## Single-unit energy auction framework</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Fvk">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_Jx">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="GZR">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgb2ee96f"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m5T">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fA1">
            <p>## Multi-unit energy auction framework</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GBo">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qs9">
            <p>So it seems you can have autonomous and non-autononmous trading</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P7-">
            <p>systems or networks.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K7J">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fX_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jeS">
            <p>&lt;a id="org8d88f27"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gJ2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="nyC">
            <p># Auction models</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7vX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="adv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1qO">
            <p>&lt;a id="org7cb3270"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ujq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zLo">
            <p>## English model</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ouc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2T1">
            <p>Open ascending-price single-unit auction</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w-w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hIp">
            <p>The auctioneer stops the auction when no new bids are received in a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dkd">
            <p>certain amount of time, and the lot is sold to the highest bidder.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="um1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="F7L">
            <p>Teixeira et al. 2021</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0Ez">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yTY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DAN">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgb5adedd"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i8q">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-0l">
            <p>## Dutch model</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y2e">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="JhO">
            <p>An open descending-price single-unit auction where the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PUh">
            <p>auctioneer sets a high enough price so that, presumably, no buyer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1Nn">
            <p>would want to buy at such price, and decrements the price at a given</p>
          </li>
          <li id="D78">
            <p>rate.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nqM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="u6o">
            <p>Teixeira et al. 2021</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QIr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="QDv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="4Nd">
            <p>&lt;a id="org79f7930"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3tG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="4uq">
            <p>## First-Price auction</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m_Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="seo">
            <p>The first-price sealed-bid auction, also known as the “blind” auction,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lbM">
            <p>is a single-unit auction in which each buyer submits a bid in a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2zw">
            <p>sealed- envelope fashion such that the information regarding their bid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="00B">
            <p>re- mains private throughout the auction process. The auctioneer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pmP">
            <p>unseals the bids and sells the item to the highest bidder. Contrary to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="avm">
            <p>the open auctions, in the sealed-bid auctions, the bids for a lot are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F-2">
            <p>all submitted in one iteration.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5fw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dyf">
            <p>Teixeira et al. 2021</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1Um">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="s60">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zZG">
            <p>&lt;a id="org0f6bb86"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XV5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="usr">
            <p>## Second-Price auction</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nxR">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="CII">
            <p>The second-price auction proposed by William Vickrey in [37], is a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="isN">
            <p>sealed-bid single-unit auction in which the winning buyer pays the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="03K">
            <p>second-highest bid, instead of its own. As in the first-price auction,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tnq">
            <p>buyers submit sealed bids and the auctioneer opens the sealed bids and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7SB">
            <p>sells the item to the highest bidder.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4b2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="elg">
            <p>Teixeira et al. 2021</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lZU">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7Wn">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A3P">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgfcc613f"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MMV">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="GzW">
            <p>## Blind</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1E9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="JJe">
            <p>Blind – this is a first-price sealed-bid auction where the lot is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yd1">
            <p>known by participants and where each participant can make a unique</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uIT">
            <p>individual and sealed bid, then the auctioneer opens the sealed bids</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HI4">
            <p>and the highest bidder wins the lot and pays the presented bid;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="18h">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="uc-">
            <p>L. Gomes et al.: Multi-Agent Microgrid Management System for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WtJ">
            <p>Single-Board Computers: Case Study on Peer-to-Peer Energy Trading</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EAf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="EdC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="z8A">
            <p>&lt;a id="org5e2b4b4"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3ep">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="4k7">
            <p>## Vickrey</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rpk">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wKY">
            <p>Vickrey – is a second-price sealed-bid auction similar to the blind</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_5G">
            <p>auction type, but where the highest bidder pays the second-highest bid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rLY">
            <p>and not his/her bid.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nen">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ayb">
            <p>L. Gomes et al.: Multi-Agent Microgrid Management System for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P7j">
            <p>Single-Board Computers: Case Study on Peer-to-Peer Energy Trading</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cC3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="KjH">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_9o">
            <p>&lt;a id="org8eacf19"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t5b">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fro">
            <p>## Islanded mode</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3HJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kJc">
            <p>Depending on its configuration, a microgrid can work con- nected to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w1r">
            <p>the grid or in islanded mode; i.e. disconnected from the main grid.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eP2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="f6J">
            <p>L. Gomes et al.: Multi-Agent Microgrid Management System for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eJK">
            <p>Single-Board Computers: Case Study on Peer-to-Peer Energy Trading</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rzP">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="V5Y">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="6Hq">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgcf23eb3"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pd5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jzu">
            <p># Multi-agent systems (MAS)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XF3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="boJ">
            <p>So MASActress, C# library literally translates or stands for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vNK">
            <p>"Multi-agent system actress".</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SO-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="YjT">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pPV">
            <p>&lt;a id="org8597b5f"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CvW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="clo">
            <p>## μGIM</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zcT">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="L-s">
            <p>What is this? MicroGIM?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8AW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="8tL">
            <p>Seems to be a console interface for the Microgrid framework.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mWi">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0-K">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3U1">
            <p>&lt;a id="orge2aef4a"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vv-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="BMl">
            <p>## Attributes that agents of MAS require</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hcy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="spe">
            <p>According to Wooldridge [32], agents in a multi-agent system must have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="caE">
            <p>the following abilities: reactivity, pro- activeness, and social.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NCl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="UiX">
            <p>In μGIM, all agents have these three abilities. They can react to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hew">
            <p>changes in their environments, they are responsible for monitoring and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mkv">
            <p>controlling their energy resources and they can detect changes and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eBL">
            <p>react using energy management methodologies, as seen in [30].</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fF1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="e-9">
            <p>L. Gomes et al.: Multi-Agent Microgrid Management System for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Isz">
            <p>Single-Board Computers: Case Study on Peer-to-Peer Energy Trading</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n3N">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="65J">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fV4">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgb04251a"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="J2K">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tvY">
            <p>## Game Theory</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pwV">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="U0l">
            <p>Game theory seems to be a key component of these systems.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VH1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xqZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yOt">
            <p>&lt;a id="orge968c41"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3Rt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ssB">
            <p>## DER definition</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8iV">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="YwL">
            <p>Distributed energy resources (DER)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FG5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Mw_">
            <p>W. Tushar et al.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kvZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="PVR">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="SML">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgab80567"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_OX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2nJ">
            <p>## Actors and Agents, their differences and similarities</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RFr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Vw_">
            <p>Both can perform parallel and distributed (in our case the interesting</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Dzy">
            <p>one) computation.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_ho">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="AZw">
            <p>Actors perform their tasks asynchronously. In addition, actors can</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vcy">
            <p>create other actors. Actors are purely reactive entitites. They can</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ifw">
            <p>only "react" to messages when they have been sent them.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nZz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Pbc">
            <p>Mathematics 2022, 10, 382</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XYG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hRL">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="w4O">
            <p>&lt;a id="org13f7189"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nbI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7bL">
            <p>## Sequential or concurrent runs</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zca">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="z2z">
            <p>Attention has to be paid to sequential vs concurrent execution. Which</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Avk">
            <p>will be better for the approach of this system? This needs to be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AfY">
            <p>considered. What are the implications?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XTR">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qzE">
            <p>Agent methods (that contain most logic):</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vf6">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Aa_">
            <p>-   Setup</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x97">
            <p>-   Act</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E6P">
            <p>-   ActDefault</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zqN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dJ-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ICE">
            <p>&lt;a id="org7151d59"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="H3c">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="50w">
            <p>### Setup method</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qTU">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="UzX">
            <p>This appears to be some initialisation method. It prepares the agent</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C5u">
            <p>for the upcoming execution cycle.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qum">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Kt7">
            <p>Act method -&gt; this is activated whenever an agent receives some</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3OU">
            <p>message.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AYO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lpP">
            <p>&gt; However, agents need not be purely reactive. They can maintain a state</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FyW">
            <p>&gt; and they can update it after each message, and act based on their</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lda">
            <p>&gt; overall state, not only the current message.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TQp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1Q6">
            <p>Mathematics 2022, 10, 382</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rOj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="6Lu">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="8DC">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgaf30849"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mTG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mSG">
            <p>## Important notes on choice of models</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w-d">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="RO4">
            <p>The multi-unit models (UPA and DPA) both achieved 100% of energy</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SBS">
            <p>efficiency throughout the case studies. The single-unit models showed</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m-L">
            <p>a worse performance, and no individual model consistently surpassed</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HuV">
            <p>the other three single-unit models, with the four models showing close</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7oi">
            <p>results throughout the case studies. However, the Dutch auction was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nF9">
            <p>the worst auction model on most occasions. Despite the differences</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tyd">
            <p>between the six models, the lowest daily percentage was that of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ml7">
            <p>Dutch and English models, on May 17th, sitting at 96.6%, which proves</p>
          </li>
          <li id="USC">
            <p>that all of the models per- formed very well throughout the case</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R0o">
            <p>studies, with daily values above the 95.0% threshold.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Buj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ZTi">
            <p>It seems multi-unit models are the best choice for the highest</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0HT">
            <p>efficiency.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OXd">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ZFF">
            <p>Based on this paper, the most appropriate choice for the single-unit</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7nv">
            <p>models appears to be Blind or Vickrey. English and Dutch perform</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Fy7">
            <p>poorly according to this literature.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FFr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gQi">
            <p>D. Teixeira et al.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r7e">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3_T">
            <p>It seems as though Microgrid uses the UPA auction system.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="s4M">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="oQe">
            <p>My choice of protocols then are:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yxg">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="i-A">
            <p>-   Uniform-price auction</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sO2">
            <p>-   Vickrey (Second-Price Sealed Bid auction)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9bW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tjO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="sjH">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgc786c0a"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-hp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pp8">
            <p>## GPT notes</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pUe">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hTI">
            <p>&gt; What is a uniform-price auction?  ChatGPT</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3hS">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_mO">
            <p>&gt; &amp;#x2014;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C8-">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tp0">
            <p>&gt; A uniform-price auction, also known as a "clearing price auction," is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A5i">
            <p>&gt; a type of auction in which all winning bidders pay the same</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tDB">
            <p>&gt; price. This price is typically determined by the lowest winning bid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lte">
            <p>&gt; (or the highest losing bid), depending on the specific rules of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vtZ">
            <p>&gt; auction.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VSF">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LBv">
            <p>&gt; Here is a simple example:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nOO">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3nQ">
            <p>&gt; Suppose you have 3 units of an item for sale, and there are 4</p>
          </li>
          <li id="J_3">
            <p>&gt; bidders. The bids come in as follows:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r-Y">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aO8">
            <p>&gt; Bidder 1: $10 Bidder 2: $9 Bidder 3: $8 Bidder 4: $7</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o0E">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Q-h">
            <p>&gt; In a uniform-price auction, the top three bidders (in this case,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="v_o">
            <p>&gt; bidders 1, 2, and 3) would each win one unit of the item. The price</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VVK">
            <p>&gt; that each winning bidder pays, however, would be $8, which is the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mza">
            <p>&gt; price of the lowest winning bid.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UBL">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Iq7">
            <p>&gt; This contrasts with a discriminatory auction (also known as a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="b_P">
            <p>&gt; pay-what-you-bid auction), where each winning bidder pays the amount</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Np6">
            <p>&gt; of their own bid. In the example above, in a discriminatory auction,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QkA">
            <p>&gt; Bidder 1 would pay $10, Bidder 2 would pay $9, and Bidder 3 would pay</p>
          </li>
          <li id="etc">
            <p>&gt; $8.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9hY">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gG3">
            <p>&gt; Uniform-price auctions are used in various contexts, including</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qTn">
            <p>&gt; treasury auctions and electricity markets. Their characteristics can</p>
          </li>
          <li id="U9H">
            <p>&gt; sometimes lead to unexpected strategic behavior, such as bid shading,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A3y">
            <p>&gt; where bidders bid less than their true valuation to avoid the winner's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sjx">
            <p>&gt; curse. The winner's curse refers to the tendency for the winning bid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hcr">
            <p>&gt; in an auction to exceed the intrinsic value of the item purchased,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SFI">
            <p>&gt; because the winner tends to be the bidder who most overestimates the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KSO">
            <p>&gt; item's value.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TGN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lcI">
            <p>&gt; Why are uniform-price auctions used in electricity markets?  ChatGPT</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xaj7">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fQN">
            <p>&gt; Uniform-price auctions, also known as clearing-price auctions, are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f6I">
            <p>&gt; used in electricity markets because they have certain characteristics</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i0J">
            <p>&gt; that are particularly suitable for these markets.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="j3k">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WuA">
            <p>&gt; Here are a few reasons why:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8a0">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i2P">
            <p>&gt; Efficiency: Uniform-price auctions help to facilitate an efficient</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zqo">
            <p>&gt; allocation of resources. The highest bidders (those who value the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZtE">
            <p>&gt; electricity the most) are the ones who win, and they all pay the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_N7">
            <p>&gt; same price, which corresponds to the supply-demand equilibrium in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rk6">
            <p>&gt; the market. This helps to ensure that electricity goes where it's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vgr">
            <p>&gt; valued most.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ler">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="I-O">
            <p>&gt; Simplicity: A uniform-price auction is simpler and more</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Uc0">
            <p>&gt; straightforward for participants to understand compared to other</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KG5">
            <p>&gt; auction mechanisms, like a pay-as-bid auction. In a uniform-price</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tPo">
            <p>&gt; auction, winners all pay the same price, which makes the bidding</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LFI">
            <p>&gt; strategy easier for the participants.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uT-">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YmU">
            <p>&gt; Price Signals: The price resulting from a uniform-price auction</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Egu">
            <p>&gt; can provide useful information for the market. For instance, it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Dbn">
            <p>&gt; can provide clear signals about the state of supply and demand. If</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jry">
            <p>&gt; the auction price is high, it indicates that demand is exceeding</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o4s">
            <p>&gt; supply, which can motivate suppliers to increase their production,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tox">
            <p>&gt; or incentivize consumers to reduce their consumption, thereby</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3sW">
            <p>&gt; helping to bring the market back into balance.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zNO">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NF9">
            <p>&gt; Transparency and Fairness: With uniform-price auctions, each</p>
          </li>
          <li id="doo">
            <p>&gt; bidder pays the same price per unit, which can be seen as a fair</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DzE">
            <p>&gt; method of pricing. It also increases transparency because it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7UI">
            <p>&gt; avoids scenarios where different buyers pay different prices for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T8v">
            <p>&gt; the same product.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K3m">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8T1">
            <p>&gt; Encourages Competition: This format encourages suppliers to bid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JmA">
            <p>&gt; their marginal costs, making the market more competitive and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-1Q">
            <p>&gt; possibly lowering the overall price of electricity.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SQ0">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QEs">
            <p>&gt; Reducing the Winner's Curse: The uniform price auction can lessen</p>
          </li>
          <li id="16E">
            <p>&gt; the impact of the winner's curse, where the winning bidder</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QZa">
            <p>&gt; overpays for the item. If the price is set by the highest losing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lE-">
            <p>&gt; bid, then winners are less likely to overpay.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T51">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lYq">
            <p>&gt; It's important to note, however, that while uniform-price auctions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dHn">
            <p>&gt; have these advantages, they also have potential disadvantages, such as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="erL">
            <p>&gt; encouraging bid shading where bidders bid less than their true value</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nki">
            <p>&gt; to avoid overpaying. These pros and cons need to be weighed when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jHo">
            <p>&gt; deciding on the auction format for a particular market.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gmx">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2f_">
            <p>&gt; Out of the following auction types, which would you choose if you had</p>
          </li>
          <li id="69b">
            <p>&gt; to choose (for an electricity market bidding system): English, Dutch,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JjW">
            <p>&gt; Blind or Vickrey ChatGPT</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WTn">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JG6">
            <p>&gt; Each of these auction types has strengths and weaknesses and is best</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z6B">
            <p>&gt; suited for certain situations. Here's a brief rundown of each type:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dya">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cFi">
            <p>&gt; English Auction: Also known as an open ascending price auction,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h9f">
            <p>&gt; this is the most common form of auction in use today. Bidders bid</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o_9">
            <p>&gt; against one another, with each subsequent bid required to be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2iC">
            <p>&gt; higher than the previous bid. The auction ends when no participant</p>
          </li>
          <li id="b7O">
            <p>&gt; is willing to bid further. While this method encourages</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RNf">
            <p>&gt; competition and often leads to a high final bid, it might be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9o7">
            <p>&gt; inefficient for an electricity market due to the continuous nature</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jGS">
            <p>&gt; of electricity supply and demand.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pWP">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rWR">
            <p>&gt; Dutch Auction: In a Dutch auction, the auctioneer starts with a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T6c">
            <p>&gt; high asking price which is lowered until some participant is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="weG">
            <p>&gt; willing to accept the auctioneer's price, or a predetermined</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Oc8">
            <p>&gt; minimum price is reached. This type of auction is fast but might</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IQS">
            <p>&gt; not yield the highest possible price because it may end as soon as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SBt">
            <p>&gt; the first bid is made. In the context of an electricity market, a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0R5">
            <p>&gt; Dutch auction may not be ideal due to the lack of competition for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8dy">
            <p>&gt; prices.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OtB">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h0E">
            <p>&gt; Blind Auction: Also known as a first-price sealed-bid auction, in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k4H">
            <p>&gt; this method, all bidders simultaneously submit sealed bids, so</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7r4">
            <p>&gt; that no bidder knows the bid of any other participant. The highest</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A9g">
            <p>&gt; bidder wins and pays the price they submitted. While this method</p>
          </li>
          <li id="c1I">
            <p>&gt; is straightforward, it might not lead to efficient price</p>
          </li>
          <li id="c4_">
            <p>&gt; discovery, as bidders have to bid strategically, often</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A9p">
            <p>&gt; underbidding to avoid the winner's curse.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jkw">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kgU">
            <p>&gt; Vickrey Auction: This is a type of sealed-bid auction. Bidders</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Eo">
            <p>&gt; submit written bids without knowing the bid of the other people in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pAm">
            <p>&gt; the auction. The highest bidder wins but the price paid is the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sBo">
            <p>&gt; second-highest bid. This encourages bidders to bid their true</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t01">
            <p>&gt; values, which could be advantageous for the electricity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E_5">
            <p>&gt; market. But the Vickrey auction can be more complicated for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mrE">
            <p>&gt; participants to understand.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6HK">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Mb">
            <p>&gt; Given these options for an electricity market, a Vickrey auction might</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nqS">
            <p>&gt; be most suitable. It promotes truth-telling, as bidders are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k4R">
            <p>&gt; incentivized to bid their true values. This feature could be useful in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wXy">
            <p>&gt; electricity markets where the goal is to align the auction price with</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CBj">
            <p>&gt; the real economic value of the electricity. However, it is crucial to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ctg">
            <p>&gt; note that the choice of auction design can depend on many factors</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W0a">
            <p>&gt; specific to the market structure and the participants involved.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fSd">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jcH">
            <p>&gt; In the real world, many electricity markets use a form of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iIv">
            <p>&gt; uniform-price auction, which is slightly different than these four</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6jB">
            <p>&gt; types, where the price is set at the intersection of the supply and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h0H">
            <p>&gt; demand curves for each time period.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ySa">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g0m">
            <p>&gt; Please note that the choice of an auction type in a real-world setting</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lVP">
            <p>&gt; should be made with thorough analysis and consultation with experts.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yE7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jsv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="UgR">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgdf1705a"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JhW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yPE">
            <p>## Sequence diagram and structure for Vickrey Auction model:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5n0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="QQc">
            <p>&gt; In the context of your project, the messages in the sequence diagram</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jz8">
            <p>&gt; would reflect the communication happening between the Environment</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X9-">
            <p>&gt; Agent and the Household Agents. Here's a potential sequence of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TE-">
            <p>&gt; messages based on the steps outlined earlier:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ccl">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fni">
            <p>&gt; Initialization: The Environment Agent sends an initial message to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iSP">
            <p>&gt;     each Household Agent, which includes the amount of electricity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tOA">
            <p>&gt;     needed, the amount of electricity that can be generated, and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Qdy">
            <p>&gt;     the buying and selling prices from the utility company.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_Nn">
            <p>&gt;     Message: sendElectricityData(electricityNeeds,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="434">
            <p>&gt;     generationCapacity, buyingPrice, sellingPrice)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yme">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gqk">
            <p>&gt; Bidding Preparation: Each Household Agent, after receiving the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C0L">
            <p>&gt; initial message, calculates if they need to buy or sell</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R4w">
            <p>&gt; electricity, and at what price.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7Fy">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vA8">
            <p>&gt; Bid Submission: Each Household Agent sends their bid to the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IEy">
            <p>&gt;     Environment Agent. This bid includes whether the agent is a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SOa">
            <p>&gt;     buyer or a seller, the quantity of electricity, and the price.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="V7y">
            <p>&gt;     Message: submitBid(agentType, quantity, price)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8VG">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iUM">
            <p>&gt; Bid Collection and Evaluation: The Environment Agent collects all</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oQy">
            <p>&gt; the bids and evaluates them.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4BU">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4xo">
            <p>&gt; Winner Determination: The Environment Agent determines the winners</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TyB">
            <p>&gt; based on the submitted bids.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bjv">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eY-">
            <p>&gt; Results Announcement: The Environment Agent sends a message back</p>
          </li>
          <li id="s24">
            <p>&gt;     to all Household Agents announcing the winners and the final</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ilY">
            <p>&gt;     transaction price.  Message: announceResults(winningBuyers,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pFV">
            <p>&gt;     winningSellers, transactionPrice)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-hG">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uhP">
            <p>&gt; Transaction Execution: Winning Household Agents receive the result</p>
          </li>
          <li id="opO">
            <p>&gt;     announcement and proceed with the transactions. For</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GUN">
            <p>&gt;     simplicity, you can just end the sequence here, or if</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TL2">
            <p>&gt;     necessary, you can have an additional message where the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lr3">
            <p>&gt;     Household Agents confirm the transaction.  Message:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cQd">
            <p>&gt;     confirmTransaction()</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6Xh">
            <p>&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hcj">
            <p>&gt; Please note that the actual messages might vary based on the exact</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_T8">
            <p>&gt; implementation of your project and the detailed information that needs</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Dce">
            <p>&gt; to be communicated between the agents. The above is a simplified</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i9e">
            <p>&gt; representation and might need to be tailored to fit your project's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-pQ">
            <p>&gt; requirements.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AlK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="W8p">
            <p>Different agent types involved:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pk5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dfD">
            <p>In your case, the sequence diagram for a Vickrey auction (also known</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zF6">
            <p>as a sealed-bid second-price auction) might involve the following</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9Nv">
            <p>entities: Household Agent acting as the bidder (can be both a buyer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="12F">
            <p>and a seller), Environment Agent acting as the auctioneer, and Utility</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o_Q">
            <p>Company (since it can also be a participant in buying and selling).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="H6V">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Q6j">
            <p>NOVEL PAPER GOOD REFERENCE:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6Lr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ctp">
            <p>&gt; Vickrey auction. In order to achieve incentive compatibility in the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1kI">
            <p>&gt; presence of prosumer uncertainty, we employ a variant of a Vickrey</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aQI">
            <p>&gt; auction mechanism with reserve price. Vickrey auction is known to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IdR">
            <p>&gt; maximize the social welfare, which in a single-item auction means</p>
          </li>
          <li id="988">
            <p>&gt; allocating the item to the bidder with the highest offer. The seller</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R4S">
            <p>&gt; announces the reliability probability 𝑟𝑠 of the unit of energy surplus</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DLz">
            <p>&gt; sold, and each buyer 𝑖 submits her bid 𝑏𝑖 to obtain this unit. The</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zp9">
            <p>&gt; prosumer with the highest bid wins and pays a price equal to the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TcG">
            <p>&gt; highest losing bid. The seller’s minimum accepted bid (reserve price)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4Dd">
            <p>&gt; is equal to the anticipated amount of money she will receive if the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Pqe">
            <p>&gt; energy surplus indeed arises and she sells it directly to the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5f2">
            <p>&gt; grid. This amount equals to 𝑠 = 𝑟𝑠 · 𝑝𝐹 𝐼𝑇 + (1 − 𝑟𝑠 ) · 0 = 𝑟𝑠 · 𝑝𝐹</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QQj">
            <p>&gt; 𝐼𝑇 . Note that the seller is assumed to have no cost and is only</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9-X">
            <p>&gt; characterized by its reliability. If there were a cost, this would be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qoi">
            <p>&gt; included in her participation constraint, i.e. in the reserve price</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RYo">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vnY">
            <p>Angeliki Anastopoulou, George D. Stamoulis, and Iordanis Koutsopoulos.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o6R">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pYr">
            <p>1.  Efficient Peer-to-Peer Energy Trading Mechanisms with Unreliable</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x6R">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

      <li id="3MI4">
        <p>How to make it difficult to be jealous</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="E3WO">
            <p>You can make it difficult to be jealous. Here is how:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kIWP">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="us">
            <p>The next time you feel jealous, ask yourself, would you swap *every*</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wK">
            <p>aspect of your current condition with theirs? If the answer is no, you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GAu7">
            <p>can't be jealous.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wi">
            <p>To spell this out more clearly: person A may be jealous of person B's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="I6">
            <p>material assets and possessions. But person B has a crippling</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i1">
            <p>disease. Would person A so quickly swap their exact condition for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gE">
            <p>person B?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7I">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
