      <li id="awkK">
        <p>From Bill’s Philosophy Box</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="T9">
            <p>Hi Ben,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zfnx">
            <p>It was a shame you couldn't make the trip down. However, I understand</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qj">
            <p>the reasons and I think the priorities are right.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ad">
            <p>Now-THE BOX-wtf is that all about? It was intended to be a thank you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="c2">
            <p>for my birthday gift. But then the butterfly that is my mind began</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TZ">
            <p>spreading its wings. Philosophy intervened (inevitably). No point in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zd">
            <p>buying something because that is just playing ping pong with money. It</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3E">
            <p>seemed to me that a gift of time (mine) would hold more value. So</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ka">
            <p>given the tradition in the family of me giving boxes, I decided that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZE">
            <p>would fit the bill.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="M_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="nu">
            <p>Sometimes when I make a box it is a celebration of the material. It's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HFdG">
            <p>beauty or texture. Yours is a philosophy box. Hence it is made from</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cH">
            <p>scrap wood which I tried to make useful and attractive. Better, in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="My">
            <p>other words, but by what definition?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_X">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-m">
            <p>Hence we move into the realms of philosophy. The box is to be used as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ra">
            <p>a container, obviously. It is also intended to be a practical example</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SY">
            <p>of philosophy. If intended as a puzzle what elements does it contain?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2H">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="I8">
            <p>I will offer no answers. That is also a philosophical point. If, as I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B_">
            <p>hope, you try to solve the puzzles, there is a metaphysical link</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gF">
            <p>formed between you and I. What was that annoying old bastard thinking,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UI">
            <p>what did he mean?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3g">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="H9">
            <p>If nothing else it will make the gift last longer. Have fun with it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="m6I6">
            <p>Bill.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="NF">
            <p>p.s.: if you think you have found the answer to the puzzle tell me and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="b3">
            <p>I'll confirm it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="V1Yq">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="H7k4">
        <p>Popularity and quality do not equate</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="db">
            <p>I suppose it is somewhat depressing to me that quality and popularity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WNVq">
            <p>do not equate.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jg">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wT">
            <p>As in, something of high quality can be of low popularity. And</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5m">
            <p>vice versa. Upsettingly, those who have a low quality high popularity</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m6">
            <p>thing often can't see the low quality attributes, because those are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MX">
            <p>masked by the popularity.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ek">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A2">
            <p>If something is X popular, how can it possibly be low quality? This is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T1">
            <p>almost like the social engineering of Thinkspeak.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3S">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5X">
            <p>Conversely, what popularity must Y reach in order to become "high</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TK">
            <p>quality"? Can Y be high quality by virtue of its popularity?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mf">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

          </li>

      <li id="WV_g">
        <p>Flywheel</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="vRYt">
            <p>"Sometimes I run fast when I feel like it, but if I increase the pace</p>
          </li>
          <li id="j5">
            <p>I shorten the amount of time I run, the point being to let the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pf">
            <p>exhilaration I feel at the end of each run carry over to the next day.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_L">
            <p>This is the same sort of tack I find necessary when writing a novel. I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5x">
            <p>stop every day right at the point where I feel I can write more. Do</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z3">
            <p>that, and the next day's work goes surprisingly smoothly. I think</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7G">
            <p>Ernest Hemingway did something like that. To keep on going, you have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u4jX">
            <p>to keep up the rythm. This is the important thing for long-term</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QC">
            <p>projects. Once you set the pace, the rest will follow. The problem is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T0">
            <p>getting the flywheel to spin at a set speed&amp;#x2013;and to get to that point</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NpYQ">
            <p>takes as much concentration and effort as you can manage."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O5HZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2KvO">
            <p>Murakami</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pxxK">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="adh_">
        <p>Physicially exhaust portion of discontent</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Yacx">
            <p>"When I'm criticised unjustly (from my viewpoint, at least), or when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eK">
            <p>someone I'm sure will understand me doesn't, I go running for a little</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4VBK">
            <p>longer than usual. By running longer it's like I can physically</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_Y">
            <p>exhaust that portion of my discontent. It also makes me realise again</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bNul">
            <p>how weak I am, how limited my abilities are. I become aware,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ms">
            <p>physically, of these low points. And one of the results of running a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tY">
            <p>little father than usual is that I become that much stronger."</p>
          </li>

      <li id="O8uj">
        <p>Life is basically unfair</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="49qw">
            <p>"In other words, let's face it: life is basically unfair. But even in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lf">
            <p>a situation that's unfair, I think it's possible to seek out a kind of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vsyi">
            <p>fairness. Of course, that might take effort and time. And maybe it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4w">
            <p>won't seem worth all that. It's up to each individual to decide</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zd-r">
            <p>whether or not it is."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IImj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="PDqk">
            <p>Murakami</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KhIn">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="P0ub">
        <p>Old wisdom, young confidence</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="3OdB">
            <p>It seems to me there is a propensity for "older" people to become more</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MO">
            <p>stubborn because of their wisdom. Close-mindedness is natural to older</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UA">
            <p>people as body confidence and strength or vitality comes to the young.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-k">
            <p>It seems with age you must work harder to keep both physical and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qDu1">
            <p>mental aspects in check.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rEAl">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="o291">
        <p>Never take off two days in a row</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="cLmC">
            <p>The total amount of running I'm doing might be going down, but at</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VP">
            <p>least I'm following one of my basic rules for training: I never take</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C0">
            <p>two days off in a row. Muscles are like work animals that are quick on</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kn2h">
            <p>the uptake. If you carefully increase the load, step by step, they</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C_Hw">
            <p>learn to take it. As long as you explain your expectations to them by</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VgJn">
            <p>actually showing them examples of the amount of work they have to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cO">
            <p>endure, your muscles will comply and gradually get stronger. It</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iJ">
            <p>doesn't happen overnight, of course. But as long as you take your time</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LN">
            <p>and do it in stages, they won't complain &amp;#x2013; aside from the occasional</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DP">
            <p>long face &amp;#x2013; and they'll very patiently and obediently grow stronger.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wNxh">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="wsU5">
        <p>You know a book is well written when the author feels like an old</p>
      </li>
      <li id="UhRs">
        <p>friend that is by your side.</p>
      </li>
      <li id="-kc_">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="Gexw">
        <p>Raymond Chandler</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Wipd">
            <p>"In private correspondence the great mystery writer Raymond Chandler</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DG">
            <p>once confessed that even if he didn't write anything, he made sure he</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hk">
            <p>sat down at his desk every single day and concentrated I understand</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IU">
            <p>the purpose behind his doing this. This is the way Chandler gave</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nei9">
            <p>himself the physical stamina a professional writer needs, quietly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nt">
            <p>strengthening his willpower."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EOCN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="L_fu">
            <p>Murakami</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k6p5">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="3Ars">
        <p>Manual labour, mental labour</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="2sGj">
            <p>I think the following is also applicable to programming:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="en">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="C4">
            <p>"Writing novels, to me, is basically a kind of manual labor. Writing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XN">
            <p>itself is mental labor, but finishing an entire book is closer to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ac">
            <p>manual labor. It doesn't involve heavy lifting, running fast, or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wd">
            <p>leaping high. Most people, though, only see the surface reality of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="a-6J">
            <p>writing and think of writers as involved in quiet, intellectual work</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ujxu">
            <p>done in their study. If you have the strength to lift a coffee cup,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="v3Mw">
            <p>they figure, you can write a novel. But once you try your hand at it,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0y">
            <p>you soon find that it isn't as peaceful a job as it seems. The whole</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xU">
            <p>process&amp;#x2013;sitting at your desk, focusing your mind like a laser beam,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cj">
            <p>imagining something out of a blank horizon, creating a story,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_k">
            <p>selecting the right words, one by one, keeping the whole flow of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Wd">
            <p>story on track&amp;#x2013;requires far more energy, over a long period, than</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k37-">
            <p>most people ever imagine."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qM5t">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OzR4">
            <p>Murakami</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QvqG">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="m5An">
        <p>A little bit every day</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="kdsE">
            <p>From [Stephen Ango](20230716T140306--stephen-ango-on-writing-to-dos.md):</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="sL">
            <p>When trying to jumpstart a new habit, the only thing that matters is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="c0Mr">
            <p>making consistent progress.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ns">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="LPgC">
            <p>It’s easy to get in your own way by setting the bar too high. Instead,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gw">
            <p>set the bar as low as possible. Any progress at all is a good thing.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DHg8">
            <p>What is the smallest unit of progress you can make?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="sH">
            <p>Do one push up Read one page Write one sentence Take one photo</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Fx">
            <p>Draw one doodle</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BahN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Q9">
            <p>Just do one every day.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="H_">
            <p>If you can only do one per day for weeks or months, it’s more progress</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yJ">
            <p>than doing nothing. Soon enough, you’ll have done more than you could</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uNgK">
            <p>have imagined.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="Gk4J">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="UU-z">
        <p>Go slow</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="N5">
            <p>Realistically, when was the last time you regretted doing something</p>
          </li>
          <li id="e-tq">
            <p>slowly and methodically. I bet you can remember the last time you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vm">
            <p>rushed something and regretted it. Faced with the choice between slow</p>
          </li>
          <li id="y7">
            <p>and fast, choose slow.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JAcR">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="T_sa">
        <p>Dip in, dip out</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="2R">
            <p>I'm trialling a new method of work. I call it "dip in, dip out". The</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9L">
            <p>premise is simple:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="LQ">
            <p>-   4-5 hours (start with 4) of intense work in one sitting. Once I have</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="BP">
                <p>a physicial  pomodoro timer, I will track this and also integrate</p>
              </li>
              <li id="sV">
                <p>some small breaks to avoid burnout.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="1K">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="O7">
            <p>-   Once your 4-5 hours are complete, stop. Leave your desk, for your</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="ty">
                <p>day is over now. Keep Slack and other communication mediums open in</p>
              </li>
              <li id="b0">
                <p>case of contact, and, of course, you'll still need to attend</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Pl">
                <p>meetings outside this window. But cease all coding and design</p>
              </li>
              <li id="pH">
                <p>activities at this point.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="0RC3">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="ab">
            <p>The key with the intense focus would be to stop when you start to feel</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YO8Y">
            <p>[real resistance](20230806T161839--flywheel.md).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zhwU">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="VYZ3">

      <li id="kjYC">
        <p>Wikispooks</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="N0">
            <p>&lt;https://wikispooks.com/wiki/Wikispooks:About&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OrxE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="z962">
            <p>Wikispooks was established to facilitate a collective re-examination</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MW">
            <p>of recent history.[2] Since 2010 we have gradually focused our</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zr">
            <p>research on deep politics (the business of deep state groups) since</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WYoR">
            <p>this area is not subject to proper scrutiny by corporate media such as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Qs">
            <p>Wikipedia. Wikispooks aims to organise documents and first hand</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_H">
            <p>testimony as clearly as possible, carefully avoiding enemy images and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9QCg">
            <p>polarising perspectives, respecting our common humanity and looking</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p0Dz">
            <p>forward to a deep seated truth and reconciliation, as the formerly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LX">
            <p>hidden business of deep politics becomes increasingly exposed. Of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3c">
            <p>particular interest are structural deep events with official</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P8jh">
            <p>narratives[3] which cannot explain readily observable facts, such as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R4">
            <p>such as the "war on terror", the "war on drugs", 9/11 and of course</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-f">
            <p>COVID-19 and the associated injections.</p>
