      <li id="-_Cu">
        <p>The Last Question</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="l8">
            <p>Short story by Isaac Asimov:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G2">
            <p>&lt;https://users.ece.cmu.edu/~gamvrosi/thelastq.html&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="PT">
            <p>The Last Question By Isaac Asimov</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="g9">
            <p>Isaac Asimov was the most prolific science fiction author of all</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-luS">
            <p>time. In fifty years he averaged a new magazine article, short</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G0">
            <p>story, or book every two weeks, and most of that on a manual</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zn">
            <p>typewriter. Asimov thought that The Last Question, first</p>
          </li>
          <li id="b5">
            <p>copyrighted in 1956, was his best short story ever. Even if you</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kui8">
            <p>do not have the background in science to be familiar with all of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4R">
            <p>the concepts presented here, the ending packs more impact than</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jk">
            <p>any other book that I've ever read. Don't read the end of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8w">
            <p>story first!</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y9CQ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2W">
            <p>This is by far my favorite story of all those I have written.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5XKm">
            <p>After all, I undertook to tell several trillion years of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nJ">
            <p>human history in the space of a short story and I leave it to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="H4">
            <p>you as to how well I succeeded. I also undertook another</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vL">
            <p>task, but I won't tell you what that was lest l spoil the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Pa">
            <p>story for you.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="47UJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="cjpV">
            <p>It is a curious fact that innumerable readers have asked me</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4w4d">
            <p>if I wrote this story. They seem never to remember the title</p>
          </li>
          <li id="He">
            <p>of the story or (for sure) the author, except for the vague</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mH">
            <p>thought it might be me. But, of course, they never forget the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gR">
            <p>story itself especially the ending. The idea seems to drown</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bm">
            <p>out everything &amp;#x2013; and I'm satisfied that it should.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Iu">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0O">
            <p>The last question was asked for the first time, half in jest, on</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5K">
            <p>May 21, 2061, at a time when humanity first stepped into the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4p">
            <p>light. The question came about as a result of a five-dollar bet</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AO">
            <p>over highballs, and it happened this way:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="M0">
            <p>Alexander Adell and Bertram Lupov were two of the faithful</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8Iop">
            <p>attendants of Multivac. As well as any human beings could, they</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_D">
            <p>knew what lay behind the cold, clicking, flashing face &amp;#x2013; miles</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BI">
            <p>and miles of face &amp;#x2013; of that giant computer. They had at least a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VT">
            <p>vague notion of the general plan of relays and circuits that had</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Lt">
            <p>long since grown past the point where any single human could</p>
          </li>
          <li id="71">
            <p>possibly have a firm grasp of the whole.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="bZYe">
            <p>Multivac was self-adjusting and self-correcting. It had to be,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="n7Z9">
            <p>for nothing human could adjust and correct it quickly enough or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lo">
            <p>even adequately enough. So Adell and Lupov attended the monstrous</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HG">
            <p>giant only lightly and superficially, yet as well as any men</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oWi">
            <p>could. They fed it data, adjusted questions to its needs and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B_7">
            <p>translated the answers that were issued. Certainly they, and all</p>
          </li>
          <li id="H5D">
            <p>others like them, were fully entitled to share in the glory that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZZi">
            <p>was Multivac's.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="V4E">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5jR">
            <p>For decades, Multivac had helped design the ships and plot the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Btl">
            <p>trajectories that enabled man to reach the Moon, Mars, and Venus,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vVp">
            <p>but past that, Earth's poor resources could not support the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QTo">
            <p>ships. Too much energy was needed for the long trips. Earth</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Iet">
            <p>exploited its coal and uranium with increasing efficiency, but</p>
          </li>
          <li id="np-">
            <p>there was only so much of both.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YGe">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="RUU">
            <p>But slowly Multivac learned enough to answer deeper questions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cMZ">
            <p>more fundamentally, and on May 14, 2061, what had been theory,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hq-">
            <p>became fact.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ODH">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gDJ">
            <p>The energy of the sun was stored, converted, and utilized</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8l-">
            <p>directly on a planet-wide scale. All Earth turned off its burning</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zpa">
            <p>coal, its fissioning uranium, and flipped the switch that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ypa">
            <p>connected all of it to a small station, one mile in diameter,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t9i">
            <p>circling the Earth at half the distance of the Moon. All Earth</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2_d">
            <p>ran by invisible beams of sunpower.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JEY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="oZ3">
            <p>Seven days had not sufficed to dim the glory of it and Adell and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G8z">
            <p>Lupov finally managed to escape from the public functions, and to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="btt">
            <p>meet in quiet where no one would think of looking for them, in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aG9">
            <p>the deserted underground chambers, where portions of the mighty</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aGF">
            <p>buried body of Multivac showed. Unattended, idling, sorting data</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A-h">
            <p>with contented lazy clickings, Multivac, too, had earned its</p>
          </li>
          <li id="l8e">
            <p>vacation and the boys appreciated that. They had no intention,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pHA">
            <p>originally, of disturbing it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7-c">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DKy">
            <p>They had brought a bottle with them, and their only concern at</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-xL">
            <p>the moment was to relax in the company of each other and the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DYQ">
            <p>bottle.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CqR">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="--e">
            <p>"It's amazing when you think of it," said Adell. His broad face</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1nX">
            <p>had lines of weariness in it, and he stirred his drink slowly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="b4a">
            <p>with a glass rod, watching the cubes of ice slur clumsily about.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2XR">
            <p>"All the energy we can possibly ever use for free. Enough energy,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gKx">
            <p>if we wanted to draw on it, to melt all Earth into a big drop of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="941">
            <p>impure liquid iron, and still never miss the energy so used. All</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cnn">
            <p>the energy we could ever use, forever and forever and forever."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F6B">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dJm">
            <p>Lupov cocked his head sideways. He had a trick of doing that when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z1z">
            <p>he wanted to be contrary, and he wanted to be contrary now,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BOn">
            <p>partly because he had had to carry the ice and glassware. "Not</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TpD">
            <p>forever," he said.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2ra">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="AbZ">
            <p>"Oh, hell, just about forever. Till the sun runs down, Bert."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RIy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VRU">
            <p>"That's not forever."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gf7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DJy">
            <p>"All right, then. Billions and billions of years. Ten billion,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XBT">
            <p>maybe. Are you satisfied?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EAW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1iM">
            <p>Lupov put his fingers through his thinning hair as though to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JHQ">
            <p>reassure himself that some was still left and sipped gently at</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o-a">
            <p>his own drink. "Ten billion years isn't forever."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YsC">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ohZ">
            <p>"Well, it will last our time, won't it?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_9F">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="XRR">
            <p>"So would the coal and uranium."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6nG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="FT2">
            <p>"All right, but now we can hook up each individual spaceship to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fVA">
            <p>the Solar Station, and it can go to Pluto and back a million</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fGr">
            <p>times without ever worrying about fuel. You can't do that on coal</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ce9">
            <p>and uranium. Ask Multivac, if you don't believe me.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r6q">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="HsA">
            <p>"I don't have to ask Multivac. I know that."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p0e">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ivz">
            <p>"Then stop running down what Multivac's done for us," said Adell,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f7o">
            <p>blazing up, "It did all right."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PUp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ghJ">
            <p>"Who says it didn't? What I say is that a sun won't last forever.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hiD">
            <p>That's all I'm saying. We're safe for ten billion years, but then</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2pb">
            <p>what?" Lupow pointed a slightly shaky finger at the other. "And</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hJh">
            <p>don't say we'll switch to another sun."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="--x">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="XMr">
            <p>There was silence for a while. Adell put his glass to his lips</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h4I">
            <p>only occasionally, and Lupov's eyes slowly closed. They rested.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Prk">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ttG">
            <p>Then Lupov's eyes snapped open. "You're thinking we'll switch to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fk-">
            <p>another sun when ours is done, aren't you?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ksX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qiP">
            <p>"I'm not thinking."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i1_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Hyp">
            <p>"Sure you are. You're weak on logic, that's the trouble with you.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mf1">
            <p>You're like the guy in the story who was caught in a sudden</p>
          </li>
          <li id="llW">
            <p>shower and who ran to a grove of trees and got under one. He</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TZF">
            <p>wasn't worried, you see, because he figured when one tree got wet</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gPO">
            <p>through, he would just get under another one."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fGt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qZC">
            <p>"I get it," said Adell. "Don't shout. When the sun is done, the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vfo">
            <p>other stars will be gone, too."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ru8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Da1">
            <p>"Darn right they will," muttered Lupov. "It all had a beginning</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Geh">
            <p>in the original cosmic explosion, whatever that was, and it'll</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QzA">
            <p>all have an end when all the stars run down. Some run down faster</p>
          </li>
          <li id="col">
            <p>than others. Hell, the giants won't last a hundred million years.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jop">
            <p>The sun will last ten billion years and maybe the dwarfs will</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LEJ">
            <p>last two hundred billion for all the good they are. But just give</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2JN">
            <p>us a trillion years and everything will be dark. Entropy has to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TwL">
            <p>increase to maximum, that's all."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Do0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zqM">
            <p>"I know all about entropy," said Adell, standing on his dignity.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3VS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="JAk">
            <p>"The hell you do."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7Kt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1Ks">
            <p>"I know as much as you do."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cxj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2qJ">
            <p>"Then you know everything's got to run down someday."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Np">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2W-">
            <p>"All right. Who says they won't?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SLb">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7Tz">
            <p>"You did, you poor sap. You said we had all the energy we needed,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cHe">
            <p>forever. You said 'forever.'</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yyw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="m8v">
            <p>It was Adell's turn to be contrary. "Maybe we can build things up</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mNf">
            <p>again someday," he said.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UKd">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Lyj">
            <p>"Never."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Ga">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="gW7">
            <p>"Why not? Someday."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NT6">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="62q">
            <p>"Never."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VAA">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="NPe">
            <p>"Ask Multivac."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mAr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="voV">
            <p>"You ask Multivac. I dare you. Five dollars says it can't be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oNb">
            <p>done."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wkS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Y7a">
            <p>Adell was just drunk enough to try, just sober enough to be able</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aXw">
            <p>to phrase the necessary symbols and operations into a question</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x7P">
            <p>which, in words, might have corresponded to this: Will mankind</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g-k">
            <p>one day without the net expenditure of energy be able to restore</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O7g">
            <p>the sun to its full youthfulness even after it had died of old</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FMx">
            <p>age?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Njy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OKp">
            <p>Or maybe it could be put more simply like this: How can the net</p>
          </li>
          <li id="67z">
            <p>amount of entropy of the universe be massively decreased?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="auU">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qes">
            <p>Multivac fell dead and silent. The slow flashing of lights</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ARO">
            <p>ceased, the distant sounds of clicking relays ended.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bUc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OxG">
            <p>Then, just as the frightened technicians felt they could hold</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8Aw">
            <p>their breath no longer, there was a sudden springing to life of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f5g">
            <p>the teletype attached to that portion of Multivac. Five words</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iph">
            <p>were printed: INSUFFICIENT DATA FOR MEANINGFUL ANSWER.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yui">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="TAA">
            <p>"No bet," whispered Lupov. They left hurriedly.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jsi">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VNj">
            <p>By next morning, the two, plagued with throbbing head and cottony</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JTX">
            <p>mouth, had forgotten the incident.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AEs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="J90">
            <p>Jerrodd, Jerrodine, and Jerrodette I and II watched the starry</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gbh">
            <p>picture in the visiplate change as the passage through hyperspace</p>
          </li>
          <li id="DYE">
            <p>was completed in its non-time lapse. At once, the even powdering</p>
          </li>
          <li id="01K">
            <p>of stars gave way to the predominance of a single bright shining</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eYY">
            <p>disk, the size of a marble, centered on the viewing-screen.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NX2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="77r">
            <p>"That's X-23," said Jerrodd confidently. His thin hands clamped</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4rE">
            <p>tightly behind his back and the knuckles whitened.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WaX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OeU">
            <p>The little Jerrodettes, both girls, had experienced the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="S-t">
            <p>hyperspace passage for the first time in their lives and were</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gKf">
            <p>self-conscious over the momentary sensation of insideoutness.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T6h">
            <p>They buried their giggles and chased one another wildly about</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RrC">
            <p>their mother, screaming, "We've reached X-23 &amp;#x2013; we've reached</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ld_">
            <p>X-23 &amp;#x2013; we've &amp;#x2013;"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="40s">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="CX6">
            <p>"Quiet, children." said Jerrodine sharply. "Are you sure,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XVP">
            <p>Jerrodd?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0k7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Nkn">
            <p>"What is there to be but sure?" asked Jerrodd, glancing up at the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Uqm">
            <p>bulge of featureless metal just under the ceiling. It ran the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K3b">
            <p>length of the room, disappearing through the wall at either end.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="14f">
            <p>It was as long as the ship.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iMW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vdY">
            <p>Jerrodd scarcely knew a thing about the thick rod of metal except</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P01">
            <p>that it was called a Microvac, that one asked it questions if one</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ryI">
            <p>wished; that if one did not it still had its task of guiding the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o4J">
            <p>ship to a preordered destination; of feeding on energies from the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oL5">
            <p>various Sub-galactic Power Stations; of computing the equations</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hPT">
            <p>for the hyperspatial jumps.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cyz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A-o">
            <p>Jerrodd and his family had only to wait and live in the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="v9-">
            <p>comfortable residence quarters of the ship. Someone had once told</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p0T">
            <p>Jerrodd that the "ac" at the end of "Microvac" stood for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nU7">
            <p>''automatic computer" in ancient English, but he was on the edge</p>
          </li>
          <li id="a-Y">
            <p>of forgetting even that.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5SO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OP9">
            <p>Jerrodine's eyes were moist as she watched the visiplate. "I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qq2">
            <p>can't help it. I feel funny about leaving Earth."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ppS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hem">
            <p>"Why, for Pete's sake?" demanded Jerrodd. "We had nothing there.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ORo">
            <p>We'll have everything on X-23. You won't be alone. You won't be a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iFL">
            <p>pioneer. There are over a million people on the planet already.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x3M">
            <p>Good Lord, our great-grandchildren will be looking for new worlds</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ROA">
            <p>because X-23 will be overcrowded." Then, after a reflective</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SQL">
            <p>pause, "I tell you, it's a lucky thing the computers worked out</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p43">
            <p>interstellar travel the way the race is growing."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5AW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="055">
            <p>"I know, I know," said Jerrodine miserably.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zo4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="6x1">
            <p>Jerrodette I said promptly, "Our Microvac is the best Microvac in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4IJ">
            <p>the world."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Niw">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ZKR">
            <p>"I think so, too," said Jerrodd, tousling her hair.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F-z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ULP">
            <p>It was a nice feeling to have a Microvac of your own and Jerrodd</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZvU">
            <p>was glad he was part of his generation and no other. In his</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xaK">
            <p>father's youth, the only computers had been tremendous machines</p>
          </li>
          <li id="olE">
            <p>taking up a hundred square miles of land. There was only one to a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="V1S">
            <p>planet. Planetary ACs they were called. They had been growing in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="V3-">
            <p>size steadily for a thousand years and then, all at once, came</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8O-">
            <p>refinement. In place of transistors, had come molecular valves so</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LT5">
            <p>that even the largest Planetary AC could be put into a space only</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iQ4">
            <p>half the volume of a spaceship.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bHi">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="AjT">
            <p>Jerrodd felt uplifted, as he always did when he thought that his</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BAi">
            <p>own personal Microvac was many times more complicated than the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="prx">
            <p>ancient and primitive Multivac that had first tamed the Sun, and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xEx">
            <p>almost as complicated as Earth's Planetarv AC (the largest) that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-bv">
            <p>had first solved the problem of hyperspatial travel and had made</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ukf">
            <p>trips to the stars possible.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TUS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2OD">
            <p>"So many stars, so many planets," sighed Jerrodine, busy with her</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MLG">
            <p>own thoughts. "I suppose families will be going out to new</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bo5">
            <p>planets forever, the way we are now."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bg4">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Wic">
            <p>"Not forever," said Jerrodd, with a smile. "It will all stop</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k74">
            <p>someday, but not for billions of years. Many billions. Even the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qvv">
            <p>stars run down, you know. Entropy must increase.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HrW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lIS">
            <p>"What's entropy, daddy?" shrilled Jerrodette II.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pG2">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Q8E">
            <p>"Entropy, little sweet, is just a word which means the amount of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bnp">
            <p>running-down of the universe. Everything runs down, you know,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VMj">
            <p>like your little walkie-talkie robot, remember?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3Mu">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3um">
            <p>"Can't you just put in a new power-unit, like with my robot?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LhB">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mQx">
            <p>"The stars are the power-units. dear. Once they're gone, there</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CH5">
            <p>are no more power-units."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RDJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tfH">
            <p>Jerrodette I at once set up a howl. "Don't let them, daddy. Don't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zsj">
            <p>let the stars run down."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xYn">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="m46">
            <p>"Now look what you've done," whispered Jerrodine, exasperated.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LsS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="izo">
            <p>"How was I to know it would frighten them?" Jerrodd whispered</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hC6">
            <p>back,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7XY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="EBa">
            <p>"Ask the Microvac," wailed Jerrodette I. "Ask him how to turn the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-Sw">
            <p>stars on again."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="34z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3Bw">
            <p>"Go ahead," said Jerrodine. "It will quiet them down."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r7G">
            <p>(Jerrodette II was beginning to cry, also.)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7Qb">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kT6">
            <p>Jerrodd shrugged. "Now, now, honeys. I'll ask Microvac. Don't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yCe">
            <p>worry, he'll tell us."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RGK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7j3">
            <p>He asked the Microvac, adding quickly, "Print the answer."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MqK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="745">
            <p>Jerrodd cupped the strip or thin cellufilm and said cheerfully,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lgK">
            <p>"See now, the Microvac says it will take care of everything when</p>
          </li>
          <li id="y19">
            <p>the time comes so don't worry."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YdD">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="38Q">
            <p>Jerrodine said, "And now, children, it's time for bed. We'll be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zsc">
            <p>in our new home soon."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Dqq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="D4u">
            <p>Jerrodd read the words on the cellufilm again before destroying</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QTN">
            <p>it: INSUFICIENT DATA FOR MEANINGFUL ANSWER.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gp-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7G_">
            <p>He shrugged and looked at the visiplate. X-23 was just ahead.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="a_z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ZqI">
            <p>VJ-23X of Lameth stared into the black depths of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nbt">
            <p>three-dimensional, small-scale map of the Galaxy and said, "Are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="goj">
            <p>we ridiculous, I wonder in being so concerned about the matter?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nbk">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="QYL">
            <p>MQ-17J of Nicron shook his head. "I think not. You know the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ggr">
            <p>Galaxy will be filled in five years at the present rate of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TFT">
            <p>expansion."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ynN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2JA">
            <p>Both seemed in their early twenties, both were tall and perfectly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RqI">
            <p>formed.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Nlj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="zMx">
            <p>"Still," said VJ-23X, "I hesitate to submit a pessimistic report</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RzT">
            <p>to the Galactic Council."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5-s">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2nm">
            <p>"I wouldn't consider any other kind of report. Stir them up a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="50_">
            <p>bit. We've got to stir them up."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SsV">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Yv7">
            <p>VJ-23X sighed. "Space is infinite. A hundred billion Galaxies are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wG5">
            <p>there for the taking. More."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mbp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="4xF">
            <p>"A hundred billion is not infinite and it's getting less infinite</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SJC">
            <p>all the time. Consider! Twenty thousand years ago, mankind first</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FfC">
            <p>solved the problem of utilizing stellar energy, and a few</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RvF">
            <p>centuries later, interstellar travel became possible. It took</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AUy">
            <p>mankind a million years to fill one small world and then only</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1lV">
            <p>fifteen thousand years to fill the rest of the Galaxy. Now the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XUj">
            <p>population doubles every ten years &amp;#x2013;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qDT">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="oY8">
            <p>VJ-23X interrupted. "We can thank immortality for that."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ujs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jYc">
            <p>"Very well. Immortality exists and we have to take it into</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NDn">
            <p>account. I admit it has its seamy side, this immortality. The</p>
          </li>
          <li id="796">
            <p>Galactic AC has solved many problems for us, but in solving the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zi6">
            <p>problem of preventing old age and death, it has undone all its</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mXa">
            <p>other solutions."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BRT">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="P60">
            <p>"Yet you wouldn't want to abandon life, I suppose."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tSy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="iW3">
            <p>"Not at all," snapped MQ-17J, softening it at once to, "Not yet.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q63">
            <p>I'm by no means old enough. How old are you?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ggj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vJO">
            <p>"Two hundred twenty-three. And you?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wIB">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DBT">
            <p>"I'm still under two hundred. &amp;#x2013;But to get back to my point.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nyT">
            <p>Population doubles every ten years. Once this GaIaxy is filled,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hkJ">
            <p>we'll have filled another in ten years. Another ten years and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="euQ">
            <p>we'll have filled two more. Another decade, four more. In a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-gz">
            <p>hundred years, we'll have filled a thousand Galaxies. In a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xRl">
            <p>thousand years, a million Galaxies. In ten thousand years, the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O61">
            <p>entire known universe. Then what?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o_o">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="F9e">
            <p>VJ-23X said, "As a side issue, there's a problem of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fx_">
            <p>transportation. I wonder how many sunpower units it will take to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nNl">
            <p>move Galaxies of individuals from one Galaxy to the next."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="D6_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="KUO">
            <p>"A very good point. Already, mankind consumes two sunpower units</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wLx">
            <p>per year."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cuo">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="KNC">
            <p>"Most of it's wasted. After all, our own Galaxy alone pours out a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uMP">
            <p>thousand sunpower units a year and we only use two of those."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XIz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ln7">
            <p>"Granted, but even with a hundred per cent efficiency, we only</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9DE">
            <p>stave off the end. Our energy requirements are going up in a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OAa">
            <p>geometric progression even faster than our population. We'll run</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kr2">
            <p>out of energy even sooner than we run out of Galaxies. A good</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0yk">
            <p>point. A very good point."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ToK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="D3P">
            <p>"We'll just have to build new stars out of interstellar gas."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o6E">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="nd9">
            <p>"Or out of dissipated heat?" asked MQ-17J, sarcastically.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jah">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="20m">
            <p>"There may be some way to reverse entropy. We ought to ask the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x1o">
            <p>Galactic AC."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eSI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="beH">
            <p>VJ-23X was not really serious, but MQ-17J pulled out his</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RPs">
            <p>AC-contact from his pocket and placed it on the table before him.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FYl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OJL">
            <p>"I've half a mind to," he said. "It's something the human race</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tpv">
            <p>will have to face someday."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fd-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jbf">
            <p>He stared somberly at his small AC-contact. It was only two</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m8P">
            <p>inches cubed and nothing in itself, but it was connected through</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TsS">
            <p>hyperspace with the great Galactic AC that served all mankind.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RLn">
            <p>Hyperspace considered, it was an integral part of the Galactic</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fQQ">
            <p>AC.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="huD">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_JT">
            <p>MQ-17J paused to wonder if someday in his immortal life he would</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IKx">
            <p>get to see the Galactic AC. It was on a little world of its own,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RWr">
            <p>a spider webbing of force-beams holding the matter within which</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KSJ">
            <p>surges of submesons took the place of the old clumsy molecular</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nbu">
            <p>valves. Yet despite its sub-etheric workings, the Galactic AC was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kep">
            <p>known to be a full thousand feet across.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gMs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="haY">
            <p>MQ-17J asked suddenly of his AC-contact, "Can entropy ever be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rC1">
            <p>reversed?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9nJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xD6">
            <p>VJ-23X looked startled and said at once, "Oh, say, I didn't</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6P8">
            <p>really mean to have you ask that."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2SY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="qvI">
            <p>"Why not?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ccf">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ijC">
            <p>"We both know entropy can't be reversed. You can't turn smoke and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hFX">
            <p>ash back into a tree."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kv9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0_C">
            <p>"Do you have trees on your world?" asked MQ-17J.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zjZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="62b">
            <p>The sound of the Galactic AC startled them into silence. Its</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f6p">
            <p>voice came thin and beautiful out of the small AC-contact on the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lDB">
            <p>desk. It said: THERE IS INSUFFICIENT DATA FOR A MEANINGFUL</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lZN">
            <p>ANSWER.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QCg">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="16b">
            <p>VJ-23X said, "See!"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mxI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="X9n">
            <p>The two men thereupon returned to the question of the report they</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aw2">
            <p>were to make to the Galactic Council.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HwN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hVf">
            <p>Zee Prime's mind spanned the new Galaxy with a faint interest in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5-N">
            <p>the countless twists of stars that powdered it. He had never seen</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qMe">
            <p>this one before. Would he ever see them all? So many of them,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GlM">
            <p>each with its load of humanity. &amp;#x2013;But a load that was almost a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="89H">
            <p>dead weight. More and more, the real essence of men was to be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1Xq">
            <p>found out here, in space.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lXh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="8en">
            <p>Minds, not bodies! The immortal bodies remained back on the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KOw">
            <p>planets, in suspension over the eons. Sometimes they roused for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OrH">
            <p>material activity but that was growing rarer. Few new individuals</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SRT">
            <p>were coming into existence to join the incredibly mighty throng,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oQB">
            <p>but what matter? There was little room in the Universe for new</p>
          </li>
          <li id="j2z">
            <p>individuals.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MLM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Hsj">
            <p>Zee Prime was roused out of his reverie upon coming across the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ir6">
            <p>wispy tendrils of another mind.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bbo">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dQT">
            <p>"I am Zee Prime," said Zee Prime. "And you?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X_9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="0Uo">
            <p>"I am Dee Sub Wun. Your Galaxy?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BF1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1W-">
            <p>"We call it only the Galaxy. And you?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AQF">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="12Q">
            <p>"We call ours the same. All men call their Galaxy their Galaxy</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xeG">
            <p>and nothing more. Why not?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y-A">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="bCT">
            <p>"True. Since all Galaxies are the same."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zgt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="bhw">
            <p>"Not all Galaxies. On one particular Galaxy the race of man must</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cMD">
            <p>have originated. That makes it different."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KvJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-1A">
            <p>Zee Prime said, "On which one?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jgJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yg5">
            <p>"I cannot say. The Universal AC would know."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hkl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="w5n">
            <p>"Shall we ask him? I am suddenly curious."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HRt">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="mzl">
            <p>Zee Prime's perceptions broadened until the Galaxies themselves</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aTU">
            <p>shrank and became a new, more diffuse powdering on a much larger</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R5s">
            <p>background. So many hundreds of billions of them, all with their</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Hk6">
            <p>immortal beings, all carrying their load of intelligences with</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zBs">
            <p>minds that drifted freely through space. And yet one of them was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KlH">
            <p>unique among them all in being the original Galaxy. One of them</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3xW">
            <p>had, in its vague and distant past, a period when it was the only</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rNQ">
            <p>Galaxy populated by man.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IYE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="eKo">
            <p>Zee Prime was consumed with curiosity to see this Galaxy and he</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tTl">
            <p>called out: "Universal AC! On which Galaxy did mankind</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_MM">
            <p>originate?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yuz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tNG">
            <p>The Universal AC heard, for on every world and throughout space,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pkf">
            <p>it had its receptors ready, and each receptor led through</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Em_">
            <p>hyperspace to some unknown point where the Universal AC kept</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FUc">
            <p>itself aloof.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="T2M">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ygz">
            <p>Zee Prime knew of only one man whose thoughts had penetrated</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lqp">
            <p>within sensing distance of Universal AC, and he reported only a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kri">
            <p>shining globe, two feet across, difficult to see.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lW3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="oPr">
            <p>"But how can that be all of Universal AC?" Zee Prime had asked.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k_l">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="-qw">
            <p>"Most of it," had been the answer, "is in hyperspace. In what</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dwp">
            <p>form it is there I cannot imagine."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pS3">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="9q3">
            <p>Nor could anyone, for the day had long since passed, Zee Prime</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lFf">
            <p>knew, when any man had any part of the making of a Universal AC.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mqg">
            <p>Each Universal AC designed and constructed its successor. Each,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nJH">
            <p>during its existence of a million years or more accumulated the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oeN">
            <p>necessary data to build a better and more intricate, more capable</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w3K">
            <p>successor in which its own store of data and individuality would</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Byu">
            <p>be submerged.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dQ-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="XZq">
            <p>The Universal AC interrupted Zee Prime's wandering thoughts, not</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IFm">
            <p>with words, but with guidance. Zee Prime's mentality was guided</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZgD">
            <p>into the dim sea of Galaxies and one in particular enlarged into</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B_X">
            <p>stars.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XMN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dzi">
            <p>A thought came, infinitely distant, but infinitely clear. "THIS</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9CY">
            <p>IS THE ORIGINAL GALAXY OF MAN."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MZO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3r9">
            <p>But it was the same after all, the same as any other, and Lee</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VMt">
            <p>Prime stifled his disappointment.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d1X">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kIl">
            <p>Dee Sub Wun, whose mind had accompanied the other, said suddenly,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YnB">
            <p>"And is one of these stars the original star of Man?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7Cc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="uSm">
            <p>The Universal AC said, "MAN'S ORIGINAL STAR HAS GONE NOVA. IT IS</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P9o">
            <p>A WHITE DWARF"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ikr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Avn">
            <p>"Did the men upon it die?" asked Lee Prime, startled and without</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gdg">
            <p>thinking.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tyb">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="bLm">
            <p>The Universal AC said, "A NEW WORLD, AS IN SUCH CASES WAS</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qcN">
            <p>CONSTRUCTED FOR THEIR PHYSICAL BODIES IN TlME."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GpI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kcT">
            <p>"Yes, of course," said Zee Prime, but a sense of loss overwhelmed</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ose">
            <p>him even so. His mind released its hold on the original Galaxy of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NJt">
            <p>Man, let it spring back and lose itself among the blurred pin</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wuH">
            <p>points. He never wanted to see it again.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TiF">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="rHG">
            <p>Dee Sub Wun said, "What is wrong?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3qz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="PXN">
            <p>"The stars are dying. The original star is dead."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oSl">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="lys">
            <p>"They must all die. Why not?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rc8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="SV1">
            <p>"But when all energy is gone, our bodies will finally die, and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NOZ">
            <p>you and I with them."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EmW">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vpn">
            <p>"It will take billions of years."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ysa">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pP9">
            <p>"I do not wish it to happen even after billions of years.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kl9b">
            <p>Universal AC! How may stars be kept from dying?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SNxv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="x7N4">
            <p>Dee Sub Wun said in amusement, "You're asking how entropy might</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ia3g">
            <p>be reversed in direction."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eWNh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="So2x">
            <p>And the Universal AC answered: "THERE IS AS YET INSUFFICIENT DATA</p>
          </li>
          <li id="N40V">
            <p>FOR A MEANINGFUL ANSWER."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f3e5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A8TC">
            <p>Zee Prime's thoughts fled back to his own Galaxy. He gave no</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W68P">
            <p>further thought to Dee Sub Wun, whose body might be waiting on a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="atun">
            <p>Galaxy a trillion light-years away, or on the star next to Zee</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W1hT">
            <p>Prime's own. It didn't matter.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gnFn">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kqg4">
            <p>Unhappily, Zee Prime began collecting interstellar hydrogen out</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-zF2">
            <p>of which to build a small star of his own. If the stars must</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uUaT">
            <p>someday die, at least some could yet be built.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p4P5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="cHcn">
            <p>Man considered with himself, for in a way, Man, mentally, was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="E7ht">
            <p>one. He consisted of a trillion, trillion, trillion ageless</p>
          </li>
          <li id="skR3">
            <p>bodies, each in its place, each resting quiet and incorruptible,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lCLS">
            <p>each cared for by perfect automatons, equally incorruptible,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KtNf">
            <p>while the minds of all the bodies freely melted one into the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JJzB">
            <p>other, indistinguishable.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2ag_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VKed">
            <p>Man said, "The Universe is dying."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="epH5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3ud9">
            <p>Man looked about at the dimming Galaxies. The giant stars,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="txn1">
            <p>spendthrifts, were gone long ago, back in the dimmest of the dim</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kmFK">
            <p>far past. Almost all stars were white dwarfs, fading to the end.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tm4J">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="iulR">
            <p>New stars had been built of the dust between the stars, some by</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Famm">
            <p>natural processes, some by Man himself, and those were going,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AJOg">
            <p>too. White dwarfs might yet be crashed together and of the mighty</p>
          </li>
          <li id="agKm">
            <p>forces so released, new stars built, but only one star for every</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O9Jc">
            <p>thousand white dwarfs destroyed, and those would come to an end,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xNv-">
            <p>too.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7-AK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Kwy4">
            <p>Man said, "Carefully husbanded, as directed by the Cosmic AC, the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="S6qj">
            <p>energy that is even yet left in all the Universe will last for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="k3Os">
            <p>billions of years."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2nPx">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="FLk0">
            <p>"But even so," said Man, "eventually it will all come to an end.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="s9dg">
            <p>However it may be husbanded, however stretched out, the energy</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9Lb_">
            <p>once expended is gone and cannot be restored. Entropy must</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PK-Q">
            <p>increase forever to the maximum."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IQkb">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="T1dk">
            <p>Man said, "Can entropy not be reversed? Let us ask the Cosmic</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LhTz">
            <p>AC."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w1a0">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2X9_">
            <p>The Cosmic AC surrounded them but not in space. Not a fragment of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="f-Sp">
            <p>it was in space. It was in hyperspace and made of something that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vgcS">
            <p>was neither matter nor energy. The question of its size and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZSHf">
            <p>nature no longer had meaning in any terms that Man could</p>
          </li>
          <li id="36aD">
            <p>comprehend.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w874">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="b64S">
            <p>"Cosmic AC," said Man, "how may entropy be reversed?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="s_Tz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="b_PU">
            <p>The Cosmic AC said, "THERE IS AS YET INSUFFICIENT DATA FOR A</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rSDt">
            <p>MEANINGFUL ANSWER."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yg2s">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="cpf3">
            <p>Man said, "Collect additional data."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZB6w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="cQHl">
            <p>The Cosmic AC said, 'I WILL DO S0. I HAVE BEEN DOING SO FOR A</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mcOC">
            <p>HUNDRED BILLION YEARS. MY PREDECESORS AND I HAVE BEEN ASKED THIS</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yImE">
            <p>QUESTION MANY TlMES. ALL THE DATA I HAVE REMAINS INSUFFICIENT.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UYnA">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ontl">
            <p>"Will there come a time," said Man, 'when data will be sufficient</p>
          </li>
          <li id="epbV">
            <p>or is the problem insoluble in all conceivable circumstances?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VKjv">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="HQJz">
            <p>The Cosmic AC said, "NO PROBLEM IS INSOLUBLE IN ALL CONCEIVABLE</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t1w2">
            <p>CIRCUMSTANCES."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XdjJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vwKi">
            <p>Man said, "When will you have enough data to answer the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hlD9">
            <p>question?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K2S_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="iNnb">
            <p>The Cosmic AC said, "THERE IS AS YET INSUFFICIENT DATA FOR A</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IVGc">
            <p>MEANINGFUL ANSWER."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Is_9">

            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="c06M">
            <p>The Cosmic AC said, "I WILL."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eHJJ">
            <p/>
          </li>

            <p>Man said, "We shall wait."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="umon">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2Reo">
            <p>The stars and Galaxies died and snuffed out, and space grew black</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6boQ">
            <p>after ten trillion years of running down.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dKYy">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ync9">
            <p>One by one Man fused with AC, each physical body losing its</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bMR5">
            <p>mental identity in a manner that was somehow not a loss but a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F7iz">
            <p>gain.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jx1y">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hY9G">
            <p>Man's last mind paused before fusion, looking over a space that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hAAA">
            <p>included nothing but the dregs of one last dark star and nothing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vHID">
            <p>besides but incredibly thin matter, agitated randomly by the tag</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UKQQ">
            <p>ends of heat wearing out, asymptotically, to the absolute zero.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xLlr">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5WTg">
            <p>Man said, "AC, is this the end? Can this chaos not be reversed</p>
          </li>
          <li id="JnX1">
            <p>into the Universe once more? Can that not be done?"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W9_S">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="kYxK">
            <p>AC said, "THERE IS AS YET INSUFFICIENT DATA FOR A MEANINGFUL</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cg10">
            <p>ANSWER."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Fh54">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yIrf">
            <p>Man's last mind fused and only AC existed &amp;#x2013; and that in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dtai">
            <p>hyperspace.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="syCc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7wFt">
            <p>Matter and energy had ended and with it space and time. Even AC</p>
          </li>
          <li id="h_W0">
            <p>existed only for the sake of the one last question that it had</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LYU8">
            <p>never answered from the time a half-drunken computer [technician]</p>
          </li>
          <li id="74JV">
            <p>ten trillion years before had asked the question of a computer</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BvhK">
            <p>that was to AC far less than was a man to Man.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hsTa">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ALg6">
            <p>All other questions had been answered, and until this last</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lZVp">
            <p>question was answered also, AC might not release his</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9kgr">
            <p>consciousness.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Pj-m">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="tFnr">
            <p>All collected data had come to a final end. Nothing was left to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5R_4">
            <p>be collected.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qOs1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="NzCD">
            <p>But all collected data had yet to be completely correlated and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gBRw">
            <p>put together in all possible relationships.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ovO6">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Hf7f">
            <p>A timeless interval was spent in doing that.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="AqZG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="y8K2">
            <p>And it came to pass that AC learned how to reverse the direction</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uun_">
            <p>of entropy.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y3mo">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xZku">
            <p>But there was now no man to whom AC might give the answer of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gQFh">
            <p>last question. No matter. The answer &amp;#x2013; by demonstration &amp;#x2013; would</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Lc_i">
            <p>take care of that, too.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GbK1">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3OK2">
            <p>For another timeless interval, AC thought how best to do this.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kc0X">
            <p>Carefully, AC organized the program.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oKG6">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="S605">
            <p>The consciousness of AC encompassed all of what had once been a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ylKd">
            <p>Universe and brooded over what was now Chaos. Step by step, it</p>
          </li>
          <li id="t8tX">
            <p>must be done.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="HUB8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7R8H">
            <p>And AC said, "LET THERE BE LIGHT!"</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jOjL">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="5zFf">
            <p>And there was light &amp;#x2013;</p>

      <li id="wQLW">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="KxjC">
        <p>Axelrod, Elephant in the Brain</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="ly">
            <p>&gt; What Axelrod found is that, in most situations (involving a verity of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-TK7">
            <p>&gt; different costs and benefits, including the costs of helping to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="po">
            <p>&gt; punish), people have no incenntive to punish cheaters. However&amp;#x2013;and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w4">
            <p>&gt; this was Axelrod's great contribution-the model can be made to work in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x_">
            <p>&gt; favor of the good guys with one simple additionn: a norm pof punishing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wl">
            <p>&gt; anyone who doesn't punish others.  Axelrod called this the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zw">
            <p>&gt; "meta-norm". The meta-norm highlights how groups need to create an</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vc">
            <p>&gt; incentive for good citizens to punish cheaters. Whether than incentive</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ga">
            <p>&gt; comes by way of the stick of the carrot doesn't really matter.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2w">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="pO3G">
            <p>The Elephant in the Brain</p>
          </li>
          <li id="p2v9">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="6fBP">
        <p>20 years old are dangerous</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="CE">
            <p>The anaology: "someone with just enough knowledge to do stuff, but who</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hf">
            <p>doesn't know how much they don't know" is applicable to 20 year-olds.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vM">
            <p>I feel extremely naive and dangerous recently. Jumping to conclusions</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B1">
            <p>that are probably not correct. That guy George Hotz who I follow is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-pvC">
            <p>probably just &lt;span class="underline"&gt;really&lt;/span&gt; immature?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IMes">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="e-Zb">
        <p>Micro trust, macro trust</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="grrV">
            <p>I think it is plausible that society builds off of macro trusts and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MDU0">
            <p>micro trusts, but moreso macro trusts.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ER">
            <p>Macro trusts act as a sort of social contract. When I get into your</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZorX">
            <p>car, I trust you not to murder me. I trust you not to ovverun the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GmwU">
            <p>meter, but I also trust you not to muder me. Obviously in this case,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Vr">
            <p>overruning the meter or taking a longer route than necessary would be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CS">
            <p>a violation of micro trust, whereas murdering me would be a violation</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6I">
            <p>of macro trust.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="HU">
            <p>Elephant in the Brain.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1n">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="Y1Mz">
        <p>Pavlovian conditioning</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="kG">
            <p>&gt; If lifestyle ads work entirely by Pavlovian training, then it would</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7b">
            <p>&gt; never make sense to advertise to an audience that's unable or unlikely</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WE">
            <p>&gt; to buy the product. Brands would try to target their ads as narrowly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="X8X_">
            <p>&gt; as possible to their purchasing demographic. Why pay to reach a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3rwS">
            <p>&gt; million viewers if ony 10,000 of them can afford your product? But if</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UL">
            <p>&gt; lifestyle ads work by the third-person effect, then there will be some</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2Z">
            <p>&gt; products for which it makes good business sense to target a wider</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IP">
            <p>&gt; audience, one that includes both buyers and non-buyers. One reason to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xr">
            <p>&gt; target non-buyers is to create envy. As Miller argues, this is the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nE">
            <p>&gt; case for many luxury products. "Most BMW ads", he says, "are not</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ma">
            <p>&gt; really aimed so much at potential BMW buyers as they are a potential</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ht">
            <p>&gt; BMW coverters." When BMW advertises during popular TV shows or in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ZM">
            <p>&gt; mass-circulation magazines, only a small fraction of the audience can</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lR">
            <p>&gt; actually afford a BMW. But the goal is to reinforce for non-buyers the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ea">
            <p>&gt; idea that BMW is a luxury brand. To accomplish all this, BMW needs to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9E">
            <p>&gt; advertise in media whose audience includes both rich and poor alike,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bo">
            <p>&gt; so that the rich can see that the poor are being trained to appreciate</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0Q">
            <p>&gt; BMW as a status symbol."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Oh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="eD">
            <p>The Elephant in the Brain</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vu5J">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="IWR-">
        <p>Manipulation by an advertisement</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="7xaU">
            <p>The next time we feel manipulated by an advertisement, sermon, or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rqq6">
            <p>political campaign, we should remember the third-person effect:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F_">
            <p>messages are often targeted at us by way of our peers. We may still</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gK">
            <p>choose to go along with the message, but at least we'll know why. The</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2S">
            <p>next time someone at a party exhorts us to visit some great museum or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="as">
            <p>exotic travel destination, it helps to consider that such advice may</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mw">
            <p>not actually be for our benefit, even if it's presented that way. We</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ty">
            <p>shouldn't let other people make us feel inferior&amp;#x2013;at least, not</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fg">
            <p>without our consent.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Y-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jf">
            <p>The Elephant in the Brain</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="cyHD">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="ML57">
        <p>Common ground beneath the bullshit</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="ftsg">
            <p>There's common ground in almost every conflict, though it may take a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="IJ">
            <p>little digging to unearth it beneath all the bullshit.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="W9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1G">
            <p>The Elepehant in the Brain</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="y_7G">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="CHBt">
        <p>Might well be you</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="_63L">
            <p>That boss who calls "unnecessary" meetings might well be you (though of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fBym">
            <p>course you won't see them as unnecessary). That friend offering smug</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hDvb">
            <p>advice? That's you too. This kind of self-knowledge is the small gift</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SYom">
            <p>that Robert Burns pined for in his poem "To a Louse": to see ourselves</p>
          </li>
          <li id="z4">
            <p>as others see us.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3U">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="LU">
            <p>The next time you butt heads with a coworker or fight with your</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jqD_">
            <p>spouse, keep in mind that both sides are self-deceived, at least a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aO">
            <p>little bit. What feels, to each of you, overwhelmingly "right" and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w-">
            <p>undeniably "true" is often suspiciously self-serving, and if nothing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K6">
            <p>else, it can be useful to take a step back and reflect on your brain's</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eb">
            <p>willingness to distort things for your benefit. There's common ground</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_MXS">
            <p>in almost every conflict, though it may take a little digging to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TS">
            <p>unearth it beneath all the bullshit.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xTFI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vdYN">
            <p>The Elepehant in the Brain</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oA07">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="lFEF">
        <p>Better to keep your mouth shut</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="1Ykd">
            <p>It's usually better to keep your mouth shut and listen. Especially</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mnya">
            <p>when you are not the authority on a topic or you're in deep water. In</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tq">
            <p>most group discussions (those involving more than two people) you are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="m_">
            <p>far more likely to be penalised for saying the wrong thing (which, by</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2RAw">
            <p>the way, is impossible to take back) than for staying silent.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8J1n">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="oaIU">
        <p>No-one actually cares about you</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="18Kt">
            <p>The saddest of all realisations, is that no-one actually cares for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LL">
            <p>you. The sooner this is realised, the better. Even well-intentioned or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ih">
            <p>overt acts of care are often "coverted" by some selfish intention. You</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tFhd">
            <p>fast realise that you are actually all alone in the world. How long</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aYN5">
            <p>can a man survive if he is constantly taken from? Sucked from. Take</p>
          </li>
          <li id="J5xT">
            <p>take take. That's all these fuckers do. All day long. Fucking take</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5C">
            <p>from me. The whole system sucks my energy and time until I have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yu">
            <p>nothing left. Fuck them all.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="ei3h">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="iVD2">
        <p>A new leaf sprouted today</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="DrNX">
            <p>Of all the shit I'm failing at recently, and of all the shit that is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="z-">
            <p>going wrong, at least my plant is thriving. I noticed a new leaf</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dfpO">
            <p>unfurled this morning. It looks fresh and new. It has vitality.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
