      <li id="R-S">
        <p>Notes on Phoenix LiveView</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="8zJ">
            <p># The basic architecture</p>
          </li>
          <li id="z9">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="fV">
            <p>My understanding is that the base architecture of a LiveView app is as</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_l">
            <p>follows (3-layer based):</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="7i">
            <p>-   Frontend code (essentially markdown files with LiveView sprinkled in?)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9p">
            <p>-   Context (boundary layer). This seems to be described almost like a</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="5q">
                <p>middleware. It protects the "core" schema layer from the frontend by</p>
              </li>
              <li id="y2">
                <p>enforicing sanitisation (in the form of what is called</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Tg">
                <p>"changesets").</p>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="Fe">
            <p>-   Core: the core interfaces with the database. It includes the data</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="BXr">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="lYT">
        <p>Phoenix verified routes</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="RG">
            <p>It is possible to use verified routes in Phoenix by appending a tilde</p>
          </li>
          <li id="41">
            <p>(~p) to them, e.g. I'm not 100% sure how this works yet but it seems</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xB">
            <p>quite useful.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B7">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="hj">
            <p>[See here](https://github.com/phoenixframework/phoenix/blob/master/guides/routing.md#verified-routes)</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="bVt">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="YR1">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="Ii3">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="Tk3">
        <p>Bill’s response to the parallel self</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Zlq">
            <p>Bill's response:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="J8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="i2">
            <p>Ben, Let me start with a caution. The areas of self and person address</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ya">
            <p>the fundamentals of human existence. Prolonged exposure, study, in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fk">
            <p>areas such as those has been known to cause depression. My caution is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nl">
            <p>if you want to continue studying philosophy, cultivate a detached</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z8">
            <p>persona to do it, an academic approach. To find personal issues worth</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YQ">
            <p>study is a valid approach but the exercise needs to maintain</p>
          </li>
          <li id="M2">
            <p>distance. Now to your conundrum:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="14">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="KU">
            <p>1.  Current state: unproductive and ungrateful</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ir">
            <p>2.  Intermediary state: do the thing (i.e. go to the office)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ei">
            <p>3.  Future state: productive and grateful</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bg">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="T8">
            <p>Are these three statements (as propositions) entirely accurate?  Point</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cR">
            <p>1 seems to imply they are not. I perceive logical inexactitude partly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SG">
            <p>due to language limitation/selection and partly due to mixing the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ua_">
            <p>objective with the subjective.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sb-">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="aAP">
            <p>You place what I will call Self 1 (S1) in a defined state. A state</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BE5">
            <p>that is currently held, by S1, to be less than ideal. Is the word</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LZF">
            <p>‘unproductive’, in this case, a comparative? Compared to who, what? If</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r8N">
            <p>the comparator is external we would have one argument if the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SfG">
            <p>comparator is internal it would be an entirely different debate.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0DY">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="vMw">
            <p>If, as I suspect, it is internal then who is making the comparison? As</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3eR">
            <p>the future self does not yet exist it must be S1. I would argue that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aKR">
            <p>progress in any situation can only be achieved at the cost of changing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eDe">
            <p>what a past self (S1x) put in place. At the time that S1x put that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="TZ6">
            <p>construction in place was it done with intellectual integrity ie the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Jhg">
            <p>best that could be achieved with the available resources? Resources</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GD8">
            <p>would include personal capabilities, temporal limitations, external</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q9h">
            <p>impositions and materials available.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lFH">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="j0N">
            <p>Assume S1x was productive within the limits imposed by the resources</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gRi">
            <p>at the time. Since the S1 person is the derivative of S1x (he cannot</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lBY">
            <p>be derived from any other person) it must argue that S1x passed to S1</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9EQ">
            <p>a situation that S1x expected S1 to view with scepticism. This is what</p>
          </li>
          <li id="CUw">
            <p>S1x did to bring about the existing situation by changing what went</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Upd">
            <p>before (from an even earlier S1 iteration) so he also recognised the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tb9">
            <p>need for scepticism.  Intellectually speaking S1 can only fail, be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KNj">
            <p>unproductive, if he knowingly fails to apply this imperative to the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Oog">
            <p>work of S1x. Imperfection is the natural state of humans. Even knowing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pLg">
            <p>this the perpetual pursuit of perfection is what brought us to where</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gLA">
            <p>we are. It is what we are, what we do. It is, to take a Darwinian</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Prf">
            <p>view, inherent to the function of being human.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BQh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xGl">
            <p>Failure (be it complete or partial) is not a negative, the fear of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="S0X">
            <p>failure is. Advance is the phoenix that rises from failure’s ashes. It</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4HW">
            <p>drives change, resolve, exploration but only with the honesty to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2PS">
            <p>accept personal imperfection. The future S1 (S1f) will be the amalgam</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0Dt">
            <p>of all prior S1x’s and S1. S1f holds potential. Einstein knew this. He</p>
          </li>
          <li id="3i-">
            <p>saw flaws in General Relativity and said of Quantum Mechanics it was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xaS">
            <p>“spooky action at a distance”, he expected holes to be made apparent</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KXl">
            <p>in his magnus opus. It was not a failure since his goal was not to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Mj7">
            <p>explain ‘everything’ but to make strides toward that goal.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F03">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="AyN">
            <p>Reinhold Niebuhr, a theologian and ethicist considered this seeming</p>
          </li>
          <li id="I5V">
            <p>contradiction and produced the ‘Serenity Prayer’.  “Lord, grant me the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RP1">
            <p>strength to accept the things I cannot change,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="B30">
            <p>the courage to change</p>
          </li>
          <li id="guG">
            <p>the things I can,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="R_2">
            <p>and the wisdom to know the difference.” As an</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2vG">
            <p>atheist I cannot accept the role of a deity however the main points</p>
          </li>
          <li id="PvE">
            <p>recognise the ‘imperfection’ of life and the nature of being human -</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yfx">
            <p>particularly the last line.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="clh">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="GxC">
            <p>For these and other reasons I would also challenge the inclusion of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rup">
            <p>the word ‘ungrateful’ and I would offer instead frustrated.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BZZ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VYa">
            <p>As to how you proceed, you have a choice but I would suggest some</p>
          </li>
          <li id="43J">
            <p>resolution is necessary. Some of that is a definition of self (which I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yQe">
            <p>would suggest you accept will be flawed). We are all prototypes of a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="S0O">
            <p>future self, constantly evolving, reacting, revising. The external</p>
          </li>
          <li id="g3k">
            <p>world will play a part. Example; we once accepted slavery. It was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="K63">
            <p>politically acceptable, economically beneficial and yet wholly</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ut9">
            <p>immoral. Those thinkers who tore down the practise were anathema to a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="sc1">
            <p>vast part of established orthodoxy. The external forces ranged against</p>
          </li>
          <li id="G1x">
            <p>the reformers were immense. It caused changes in their behaviour</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7cr">
            <p>(their person changed) which in turn caused a change in the persons</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ewi">
            <p>around them.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oPL">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yRP">
            <p>You may be frustrated with yourself. Frustration is a portmanteau</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xst">
            <p>term. Analyse it. What is wrong? The speed of progress toward a goal?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vvt">
            <p>The scope of the goal? The personal resources you can bring to bear?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SNm">
            <p>These relate to your point one, current state. Without some resolution</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WE-">
            <p>your second point, the intermediary is always going to be</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zqm">
            <p>suspect. When setting point 2 the What to do question is surpassed by</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OmM">
            <p>the Why. Why are you going to the office? There are many answers none</p>
          </li>
          <li id="lg5">
            <p>wholly correct or wholly wrong. You could answer ‘to earn some money’</p>
          </li>
          <li id="opK">
            <p>which would be correct but probably not complete. To ‘make something</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P-i">
            <p>better’? Again correct but again incomplete. We should also recognise</p>
          </li>
          <li id="2l5">
            <p>those selfish drivers like ‘to be recognised as better than what went</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0QY">
            <p>before’ again incomplete</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OX5">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="U_-">
            <p>At the risk of stating the bleedin’ obvious I am older than you so my</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hap">
            <p>perspectives are different. I can look back over 70 years and my S1</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uIA">
            <p>can look at the decisions my S1x took and form a judgement based on</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WSO">
            <p>the attitudes, beliefs of my current self. Some of those will return a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0tS">
            <p>regret. I will give an example, a serious one. I have to request that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tNf">
            <p>you treat what follows with discretion.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KqK">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="iYI">
            <p>As an 18 year old I met a woman, I Iiked her. After a few dates she</p>
          </li>
          <li id="kBt">
            <p>told me she had a 3month old baby I chose to continue the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7o2">
            <p>relationship. After a year or so I was faced with a decision. The baby</p>
          </li>
          <li id="A_h">
            <p>was beginning to form views of the world, develop a personality,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ADl">
            <p>define self and relationships toward those in her orbit including</p>
          </li>
          <li id="EqZ">
            <p>me. Social pressures (those that existed then but have changed now)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aGk">
            <p>leaned towards marriage. My choices appeared to me to be binary, stay</p>
          </li>
          <li id="MWu">
            <p>or go. I chose to stay with a consequence of marriage. It was an error</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LN1">
            <p>because I had failed to take the need for deep emotional attachment</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fi6">
            <p>into account and was responding, largely, to external pressures.. I</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jrd">
            <p>felt that I was doing the ‘right’ thing for the ‘right’ reasons,</p>
          </li>
          <li id="RXo">
            <p>consideration of the child. Twenty years down the line everything fell</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YwJ">
            <p>apart and damaged all parties involved.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="-ZS">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="VGp">
            <p>With the benefit of hindsight I would claim I hold no fault for my</p>
          </li>
          <li id="GbV">
            <p>original decisions beyond the deeply regretted failure to adequately</p>
          </li>
          <li id="N2I">
            <p>account for the importance of emotional attachment. I knew I had</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0G2">
            <p>doubts but lacked the honesty and courage to address them. Those are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KBb">
            <p>personal failings I can address now. Had I done so then I would have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QpF">
            <p>caused sadness, temporary hopefully, but I would have avoided the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Zpm">
            <p>permanent and extensive damage in later years. Sometimes there is no</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oD3">
            <p>happy outcome. The wisdom comes later. The failure (mine) is converted</p>
          </li>
          <li id="KtZ">
            <p>from negative to positive if I can show the error in my thinking and</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vnl">
            <p>pass that knowledge (flawed as it will be) to others before they find</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Z6s">
            <p>themselves making a similar critical decision. To do so requires that</p>
          </li>
          <li id="nBz">
            <p>I re-examine my actions on a regular basis and change as required. If</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ha7">
            <p>I am lucky, and chance is a factor in human thinking, I help them to</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5iZ">
            <p>understand a situation without the need to experience it. Their ‘self’</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zCY">
            <p>will have changed through an agency over which they had no</p>
          </li>
          <li id="5ip">
            <p>control.They will still hold an imperfect paradigm but it will be just</p>
          </li>
          <li id="SO7">
            <p>a little less imperfect. They will still be ‘I’ but not the ‘me’ they</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cw1">
            <p>were before. They will be one of the infinite versions of S1f that had</p>
          </li>
          <li id="842">
            <p>awaited realisation as S1 when the future became now.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="C5z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ppx">
            <p>I do hope this helps rather than confuses. I have studied ‘self’ on</p>
          </li>
          <li id="oLm">
            <p>the MA course. Whilst we all believe we know ourselves when confronted</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jqV">
            <p>with a demand for the evidence we find it to be nebulous, shifting</p>
          </li>
          <li id="S0a">
            <p>sands in the winds of circumstance. That actually isn’t a bad</p>
          </li>
          <li id="dZ3">
            <p>analogy. The Sahara exists it can be seen, touched, walked</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cj4">
            <p>across. Answering questions as to exactly where it is, where the dunes</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OYp">
            <p>are now and what will be the situation in a century, an hour or even a</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9ZS">
            <p>second from now is problematical. It will still be there, still be the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Si5">
            <p>Sahara but it will, as with humans, defy permanent and complete</p>
          </li>
          <li id="fgo">
            <p>definition.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="k7A">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="2SM">
        <p>Remove top tabs on Firefox</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="04h">
            <p>This is a good modification if you are using [Tree Style Tabs Extension](https://github.com/piroor/treestyletab).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4y">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="2E">
            <p>To hide the native tabs, you'll have to add a new file called userChrome.css and the css property visibility: collapse.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mq">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="a7">
            <p>To do this, in Firefox click on Click on Menu -&gt; Help -&gt; Troubleshooting Information or navigate to about:support in the address bar.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="YE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yk">
            <p>Under the Application Basics section, there will be a section called Profile Directory with a button to Open Directory.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="XT">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wL">
            <p>In the Profile Directory create a new folder called chrome. In the chrome folder create or edit the file userChrome.css if it already exists.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="tM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ti">
            <p>The contents of userChrome.css should be the following.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kl">
            <p/>
            <ul>
              <li id="ni">
                <p>/* hides the native tabs */</p>
              </li>
              <li id="nP">
                <p>#TabsToolbar {</p>
              </li>
              <li id="q9">
                <p>visibility: collapse;</p>
              </li>
              <li id="85">
                <p>}</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Da">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="Za">
            <p>Some optional further modifications to put in userChrome.css are:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Xn">
            <p/>
            <ul>
              <li id="-p">
                <p>/* hides the title bar */</p>
              </li>
              <li id="YT">
                <p>#titlebar {</p>
              </li>
              <li id="-8">
                <p>visibility: collapse;</p>
              </li>
              <li id="Kw">
                <p>}</p>
              </li>
              <li id="NX">
                <p/>
              </li>
              <li id="kd">
                <p>/* hides the sidebar */</p>
              </li>
              <li id="6C">
                <p>#sidebar-header {</p>
              </li>
              <li id="CO">
                <p>visibility: collapse !important;</p>
              </li>
              <li id="_4">
                <p>}</p>
              </li>
              <li id="D6">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="Kg">
            <p>[Firefix open "look up" in new tab](20221219T230229--firefix-open-loop-up-in-new-tab.md)</p>
          </li>

      <li id="3VYPV26iCRSrUjpjPJVn2" data-created="2025-12-24T09:53:54Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T09:53:54Z">
        <p>Bike must be the first piece of software I’ve downgraded. I wanted to like the new preview version of Bike 2, but I just can’t get past some of the design decisions. First of all, you cannot focus headings. This is terrible for my new workflow which relies on a single file in order to manage all documents and notes.</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="Xx">
            <p>Second, you’ve got the UI choices. When you first launch the app, you’re bombarded by two new windows either side of the editor. I did not ask for a calendar view and outline view. I much prefer being able to jump between headings quickly using CMD+P.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Qq">
            <p>It’s really a shame because the extension component of Bike 2 is quite compelling. I was even building my own extension “Trails” in orders to better integrate LLMs. Sadly it looks like it won’t work out.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bp">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="LNmL4nJJRg3EQ9osG_zSX" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="8Oydda7eZ0V4DB3vrCX6a" data-created="2025-12-24T07:48:47Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T07:48:49Z">
        <p>Trails</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="7Z4Q6J1sFYp-5hU_pyI6w" data-created="2025-12-24T07:48:49Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T08:24:21Z">
            <p>Trails is a tiny extension for Bike (macOS) that allows you to query LLMs.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="OZIw8QVu3xf67RW7RSmbg" data-created="2025-12-24T07:49:06Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T09:52:20Z">
            <p>Each query is created in a new tab, allowing for creation of new enquiries. </p>

          <li id="wd0-YBeojVVcWeJdzlUbx" data-created="2025-12-24T09:52:20Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T09:52:23Z">

          </li>

      <li id="zW27BKZmKLcO2ZCTT2MY4" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="9KMDN-wB3l1sHpAoXUHJo" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Martian quote by Andy Weir</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="BkMiPa8puRv5TbQlqP4Uj" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>The cost for my survival must have been hundreds of millions of dollars. All to save one dorkey botanist. Why bother? Well, okay. I know the answer to that. Part of it might be what I represent: progress, science, and the interplanetary future we've dreamed of for centuries. But really, they did it because every human being has a basic instinct to help each other out. It might not seem that way sometimes, but it's true. If a hiker gets lost in the mountains, people will coordinate a search. If a train crashes, people will line up to give blood. If an earthquake levels a city, people all over the world will send emergency supplies. This is so fundamentally human that it's found in every culture without exception. Yes, there are assholes who just don't care, but they're massively outnumbered by the people who do.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="o_S8ljjagSxB0DWliA5ld" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="JaKQZMIOIMIoBXtxfR-cU" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Invisible audience</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="ZqBhQyrFR6I-G0VNhZovg" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Whilst advisable to relax (especially within the confines of your own home), sometimes it is helpful to imagine an invisible audience. This is especially true for arduous tasks or chores. What would you do next if one hundred people were watching?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="yOonmJ72knNoVN3s8BYof" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="8g5NZtxj-grp9Pb_Dcpsc" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Scout Mindset</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="lVxghYxZDnZyHhymgsXba" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Reading Julia Galef’s scout mindset has broaded some of my ideas about probability.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w7BdFX7hEDiASAqUUyQ58" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="8HUlhxHRHc5QvZZdiEJTi" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>I want to borrow her ball-based thought experiment and apply it to Go stones (partly becuase this analogy is eaiser for me to visualise).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="_E_092hthJ_qI1W3xM5xj" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OmSDHqeZ_6vWvvkaRCohq" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>If you want to assign a rough confidence to any future outcome in your life, you can start with the following thought experiment:</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="j7JfGNvueTa9mRra9xH7k" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>First, take your yearly salary. Hopefully you consider this a considerable sum worth betting carefully over. Now bet that yearly salary against anything. For example: I bet 45,000 GBP that I will finish three books this month.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="axaLh8agEBr6JSplkNl3J" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
              <li id="Q0t1D12mglZlWITQOVK-A" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Once the bet has been made, visualise a jar of stones.  In this  jar, there are two stones. One is white, the other black (1W:1B).</p>
              </li>
              <li id="uvMEwp4IaF0kg1sFzTZof" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
              <li id="0fVCMGZLwJZd3hsxpUabh" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Now bet against white being withdrawn from the jar. In this case, it is a 50% probability of success (and pocketing the £45,000).</p>
              </li>
              <li id="DU5ByH4vFfjwspI1iXH2p" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
              <li id="vjY2kTCf6UEe24Bs1uWLh" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Compare your bets. Which bet do you feel more comfortable taking? If you select your original bet, this means you assign above 50 chance you will finish 3 books this month. If you select the jar instead, go back to step 2, but this time with a different ratio (e.g. 4B:1W). You can now compare against a 1/4 (25%) probability, etc.</p>
                <ul>
                  <li id="SKoY6xcNS_b5XXtQKY21N" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                    <p>Iterate on this experiment until you reach a rough estimate you feel comfortable with.</p>
                  </li>
                  <li id="u72CdQ0oxrSxWqvsMwRr8" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                    <p/>
                  </li>
                </ul>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="NH_z3xezwmgYz2GZ_QgQY" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>This problem is really hard 23 Dec 25</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="b0avSUDmuRFJ4-5UymR6I" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>4:45 am in the morning. Pretty tired but I want to get this done. I want to achieve this. If I get this working it will be a bi-directional communication of sorts between Paper and Ami, which I think is a really cool piece of tech.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ljPobkHORUmQVMTem4NNh" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>I’m working on trying to inject into Paper and directly modify the DOM via an extension. I don’t even know if this is possible. I’m quite curious to start reading the code to understand how all of this works, because it’s pretty cool. It might be interesting / fun to do a writeup of my findings. How did I even achieve this, what I did, etc.? How did the LLM do all this exactly?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FN7K5Oe15dZZMtiKTh6bq" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T08:34:21Z">
            <p>I’m using GPT 5.2, but I’m struggling to get success. The tab crashes a lot and seems to struggle somewhat.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bnLJX_vdG06MMrYA8uO3a" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3SZF1eStLcX_HZD7-aNdU" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>It’s now 7am. I want to work on a new strategy for this:</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="OhA24PiiunYJvV-Bpd_km" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>1. Instead of trying to manually extract styles from the code in Ami, remove this logic. Instead you will do something else.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="xmmz1jAqDxA1zi7LgOxBi" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>2. What you will do is this: you will first READ the data-node-id element from the Paper DOM for this node to understand how the eventual output code needs to roughly look like (basically how to conform with the Paper DOM).</p>
              </li>
              <li id="6damuReHT3LUXntvS27Wj" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>3. You will ask GLM 4.6 (model) to analyze the chat for this node. You will ask it to find the latest Paper export from the user messages.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="wneX7GnfcrFZvnEHYf596" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>4. Next, you will ask it to find the code for this node ID in Ami (grep for the Node ID).</p>
              </li>
              <li id="pw7SRGyq28f6qpQCBKBu7" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>5. Finally, it should make some output that is compatible with HTML DOM elements in the Paper DOM. This output should look exactly like the updated Ami code element (the one with the Node ID commnet), but instead of the dynamic values (text values, etc.)., it should try to insert the text values from the original Paper export.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="4aGXUACu3SfP9zZGNpCIE" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>6. The node in the Paper DOM should be replaced with this updated node.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="erSVmRUgTNmcsDw7Uhhzj" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
        </ul>

        <p>On writing 23 Dec 25</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="5cLi6AAhh_CGxn6svXtQH" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Who was it I met? Ben, from Variant, who said writing is like design. Although I didn’t particularly like the guy, I’m starting to realise how important writing is. I have a natural urge to write, and I think it’s important to stream out your thoughts. This, of course, comes off the back of journalling, which I also found to be very helpful.</p>

It doesn’t try to be anything other than what it is. It allows for some about of customisation, which is nice.</p>
          </li>

      <li id="WP1pueyq5PZQMyA2vlEZs" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>New workflow for PoppaDOM</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="09qU_OVFsdvBWqvSTMFve" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>1. Get the node ID from the URL (query param ?node=“”) and store it.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="H7pG1_6LxURrytIUHtQ9Z" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>4. If the user’s clipboard contains HTML elements and DOES NOT contain a comment somewhere with the string “Code exported from Paper”, save that clipboard content somewhere (in a store or local store)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="hQ80tTd5SF0kT1xyUIx8j" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>5. Next, do EXACTLY what the Paper’s “Copy as Tailwind” does to get the Tailwind content in Paper. You should COPY exactly the Tailwind (basically mimic / automatically execute “Copy as Tailwind” without the user having to do it).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aAKBJzqNQ33IVteztcL2B" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>6. If the user’s clipboard contained HTML elements and those have been stored, create a new Ami chat and send exactly the following prompt:</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="uI2XLMowl2brkg88CCopx" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>“Make [saved HTML clipboard] look exactly like [latest clipboard item], but only modify styling and visuals, do not modify functionality. Also add a comment above this change that contains the node ID: [node ID].”</p>
              </li>
              <li id="QaS6mg4E-Bo5YaP7oZvbN" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="RBDqMZ3IToV6yI9W9_lVN" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>7. If the user’s clipboard did not contain HTML and was not stored, create a new Ami chat and send exactly the following prompt:</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="aWBGg0RhSkqI9EMRPxEJg" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>“Grep for component that has [node ID] above it. Make this component look exactly like [latest clipboard item].”</p>
              </li>
              <li id="OFjSib2D1JxSCBilk8vww" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="gbAfhllsHL7F8fOqpIFJJ" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>8. Important to remember, we can insert [latest clipboard item] here BECAUSE I asked you to do exactly the “Copy as Tailwind” feature in Paper, which copies the Tailwind code to the user’s clipboard.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LzClbzayo-W7ELl4W1cHX" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>

      <li id="1IA-7-dlNnMKwts6A515Y" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Now writing everything in one text file 23 Dec 25.</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="2aCggu8GqT3vNsZVOi1ER" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-24T08:24:37Z">
            <p>I used to keep many files in one folder “denote”. I was using the denote note-taking service created by Protesilaos Stavrou. This worked ok. I’m now back to using Bike (not Emacs), although it is important to note that the medium is agnostic. It doesn’t matter which tool I use. My new strategy is to simply write everything down in one file. The reason I like this is because:</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="Kq0TEKIU8pHTg2GhvFOaE" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>1. It’s just a .txt file. It’s not .org, it’s not even .bike. It’s just .txt. This means it is, in theory, indestructible.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="frmI4RaEgL9xiNQ429vKn" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>2. It’s searchable. I simply open the file and hit CMD+F. I don’t have to install ripgrep or some other program to peruse over my notes. Browsing is as easy as a native cmd find.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="iksyEY2Y1GFKtiTc36pXp" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>3. It’s simple. I don’t have to think. Fritction to writing is distilled to a simple newline or return key. I tried to make Emacs into something simple and easy to use. And I sort of did. Until I didn’t. Until it became quite cumbersome. I was managing configs using Nix. This is way too complex for the task of simply jotting. This is a digital jotter after all. If I want to switch back to Emacs, I can. Easily. At anytime.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="YSZOxorAm0x2xNgdewx9Y" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>4. It’s small. I just checked the size of this file, and although admittedly I have not ported over all notes, it sits comfortably at just 12kb.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="6Yo7DMRi-MT970F7bRNHQ" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>5. As we move into the age of AI, a single text file is much easier to upload as “context” to an agent, and then the agent can sort through it etc. Probably most advisable to use a local agent for privacy reasons.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="xXmXbHdwvBTcCYn-CAEDA" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p/>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>

          <li id="K7PB5MrR3y0ASsT81f1dQ" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">

        <ul>
          <li id="bTmDrm12SO5sJ0WNMx6j4" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">

      <li id="J-J-YDxUmddueMTPbgQ0W" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Apple Human Interface Guidelines 1987</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="6iUWJojSCF0Q4IhGnKBNg" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Great document on Apple’s Human Interface guidelines. This seems to have inspired Rauno’s Devouring Details.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="1pcc6eeMBdbjhLx0CKhfg" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="vg6bv1vZ7DjXzcUptrzDB" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>On Convincing Others</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="lGcUbRMQk3eE2jUMAMwtT" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>The better your message makes you feel about yourself, the less likely it is that you are convincing anyone else.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="9vEbmT9CLLl4CiBeQQqly" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="-KfjRAKk6XFXUG2c8PC7I" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Z7Ih6PdHzk</p>
      </li>
      <li id="KIj">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="Zqq">
        <p>Bayesian inference and reasoning</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="s6G">
            <p>1.  [1. Remembering priors](#orge37bcd1)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="QZ">
            <p>2.  [2. Imagine the world if your theory is wrong](#org1af36f0)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="O1">
            <p>3.  [3. Incremental updates](#orgce38ab1)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Sp">
            <p>4.  [Other resources](#orgc88e98a)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ua">
            <p>Julia Galef has published an interesting [book](https://www.goodreads.com/en/book/show/42041926-the-scout-mindset) on this topic.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ex">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yu">
            <p>Julia also offers some interesting points on Bayesian thinking.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Uk">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="wY">
            <p>She recommends:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Rg">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Bs">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="b4">
            <p>&lt;a id="orge37bcd1"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="34">
            <p># 1. Remembering priors</p>
          </li>
          <li id="cc">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OP">
            <p>Detach yourself from the problem (e.g. what is the likelihood of X</p>
          </li>
          <li id="WU">
            <p>happening before Y entered the problem space). Think about the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gt">
            <p>*priors*, the probabilities before this occured.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vm">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="eM">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Fv">
            <p>&lt;a id="org1af36f0"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="gO">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="D1">
            <p># 2. Imagine the world if your theory is wrong</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LE">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="F0">
            <p>What would the world look like if you were wrong?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="eJ">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="yG">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="p4">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgce38ab1"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="x8">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Fm">
            <p># 3. Incremental updates</p>
          </li>
          <li id="En">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="xe">
            <p>As new evidence arrives, update your threories. You can't have</p>
          </li>
          <li id="aV">
            <p>infinity evidence, (i.e. your evidence can never have a confidence of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uS">
            <p>1 or 0). You can be 0.99999999% sure, but you can never be 1% sure.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bX">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="DI">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="Ic">
            <p>&lt;a id="orgc88e98a"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Cn">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A5">
            <p># Other resources</p>
          </li>
          <li id="82">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="k4">
            <p>Some other good resources on this topic include:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="az">
            <p>-   [How to systematically approach truth - Bayes' rule](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4hHA-oqpNig)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="LC">
            <p>-   [Bayes theorem, the geometry of changing beliefs](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HZGCoVF3YvM&amp;t=0s)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Li">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="ZJ">
            <p>My own writing on this topic: Infinity confidence.</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="y5UhVLiyYwmJfiL-xgVVl" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="xicAmTY0sE64t13ijtQm9" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Infinity confidence</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="EjL0WbubgdpUDzMrJ3JCl" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>You cannot assert *infinity* confidence. Your confidence in *X idea* should fall somewhere on a spectrum greater than zero and less than one.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wdJGVA0cy8HKL1R7fR8HP" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="1dGJILvyX4_uhEUqYT3dY" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Why is 0.9999 confidence (or inversely, doubt) preferable to infinite confidence? Because it plasticises your belief system. When your belief in an idea is malleable, you can incrementally update said belief by observing new evidence (welcome to Bayesian inference).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="NqwjGStnNdBidRlBDw9sB" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="WrSIAg6p29NO9_zGhLi4K" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Imagine your emotionally vested belief in X is a vessel. Inevitably, as new waves of evidence roll in, you may be tempted to drop anchor. Such temptation will surely grow as the waves of evidence continue to contradict your world view (or in lending to this analogy, your nautical path).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="w3wO8zm5aLfMw5NnNUHu1" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="sWBOhHNiKQt0_1FZJuI4m" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>But dropping anchor is a grave mistake. At least if you sail *against* the waves of evidence, you'll experience some resistance. After enough exertion, you might be compelled to update your ideas. On the other hand, an anchored idea is rigid&amp;#x2026; blind and obvlivious to the sea of available evidence. Anchoring equals ignorance, or active relucantance to accept the truth (ugly stuff!).</p>
          </li>
          <li id="saAj7VDuthwEvVdML7XGW" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="yPR_vtSMliDuru46lpz_B" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Leaning into confusion</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="sLGCsER_XhsTcxQedT_O9" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Leaning into confusion is about inverting the way you’re used to seeing the world. Instead of dismissing observatiosn that contradict your theories, get curious abonut them. Instead of writing people off as irrational when they don’t behave the way you think they should, ask yourself why their behaviour might be rational. Instead of trying to fit confusing observations into your preexisting theories, treat them as clues to a new theory.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pQN">
            <p/>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="O4H">
        <p>Anticipating the parallel self</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="-9h">
            <p>I'm experimenting with a new thought process. I've coined a term for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VU">
            <p>it: *anticipating the parallel self*.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Gz">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3A">
            <p>A maxim I often hear is: "your future self will thank you for doing</p>
          </li>
          <li id="rY">
            <p>X."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6B">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="L6">
            <p>But will my future self really appease me? How do I quanitfy "future"?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="mh">
            <p>This line of thought is regularly applied in the face of adversity or</p>
          </li>
          <li id="0Y">
            <p>challenge. Represented in three states, it roughly maps to:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Yp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="jq">
            <p>1.  Current state: unproductive and ungrateful</p>
          </li>
          <li id="UU">
            <p>2.  Intermediary state: do the thing (i.e. go to the office)</p>
          </li>
          <li id="da">
            <p>3.  Future state: productive and grateful</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iN">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="eP">
            <p>The problem is that my future self has the same agency to make</p>
          </li>
          <li id="d2">
            <p>excuses. Put simply, my "future" self is merely a projection of my</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ph">
            <p>"current" self, thus susceptible to the same biases and pitfalls.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Bj">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="QN">
            <p>Thinking of the future self requires discipline and imagination. It is</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xj">
            <p>far easier to satiate my current condition by anticipating some future</p>
          </li>
          <li id="M8">
            <p>reasoning (no matter how sound it may be). A convincing rebuttal of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="FO">
            <p>the situation could take the form of: "I was not in the wrong. It was</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i8">
            <p>raining outside and my hair looked bad."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="qT">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="W8">
            <p>So, here is my strategy: anticipate the *parallel* self. I imagine</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u2">
            <p>dividing my current self into two trains of thought. Both trains are</p>
          </li>
          <li id="wq">
            <p>travelling uniformly on a single track. The trick is to invisage one</p>
          </li>
          <li id="i9">
            <p>train diverging from the track. For the sake of simplicity, I'll label</p>
          </li>
          <li id="bs">
            <p>this the "bad" track.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="8Q">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="3R">
            <p>Now, it should be fairly easy to picture myself on the *bad* track in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="u3">
            <p>the exact same moment. What kind of thoughts might I muster?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="N_">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="OU">
            <p>-   "I wish I had soldiered through and gone to the office."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Kk">
            <p>-   "Now I face an unproductive day ahead."</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6W">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="A1">
            <p>The reassuring news is I took the *good* track (I am currently boarding</p>
          </li>
          <li id="r8">
            <p>the bus), meaning I can convert these thoughts into a source of</p>
          </li>
          <li id="6F">
            <p>gratitude, relief and energy. What's more, these aren't anticipated</p>
          </li>
          <li id="vD">
            <p>sources, they exist now and I can exploit them *right away*, reaping the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="4W">
            <p>benefits in real-time. How often do you actually remember to praise</p>
          </li>
          <li id="iz">
            <p>yourself for all the successful past decisions you made?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="av">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="D0">
            <p>I think this line of motivated reasoning is far more accessible than</p>
          </li>
          <li id="uL">
            <p>trying to anticipate a future self. I am present me, not me two hours</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Al">
            <p>from now.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Tp">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="dV">
            <p>I'd go even futher and suggest that this is a pragmatic strategy for</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ka">
            <p>long-term goal acquisition. Accommodate the following thought:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="Ig">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="m5">
            <p>I want to become conversational in Korean. Being optimistic, I equate</p>
          </li>
          <li id="xH">
            <p>this to a year of dedicated study. Now here's a question worth asking:</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ry">
            <p>is it easier to imagine myself a year in advance, or a few minutes in</p>
          </li>
          <li id="BJ">
            <p>advance? I don't tackle goals a year at a time, rather I incrementally</p>
          </li>
          <li id="jV">
            <p>chip away at them, day by day, minute by minute, hour by</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zf">
            <p>hour. Realistically, the further into the future I ideate, the more</p>
          </li>
          <li id="pN">
            <p>ground I need to cognitively map out. This dissonance between present</p>
          </li>
          <li id="P_">
            <p>and future invites procrasination and stasis. Where do I even start?</p>
          </li>
          <li id="zc">
            <p>At least with the diversion technique I can feel immediate</p>
          </li>
          <li id="7l">
            <p>self-gratification by opting for the textbook instead of the</p>
          </li>
          <li id="VY">
            <p>controller&amp;#x2026;</p>
          </li>
          <li id="ef">
            <p/>
          </li>
          <li id="_c">
            <p>TLDR: thank yourself for smart decisions now, not later (you'll</p>
          </li>
          <li id="q6">
            <p>forget!)</p>
          </li>
        </ul>
      </li>
      <li id="h5g5gaQ5XrktGC9BUxJzP" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p/>
      </li>
      <li id="kHF40L60Ll-EFlTmx2OVp" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>Ask People for Help</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="-DTO4cx7zB_8Y_XiXeetZ" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>The easiest way to get someone to like you is for you to task them for help. This is as effective as closely listening to what someone says.</p>
          </li>
          <li id="F9qnIW9Ab6lF707i8MQI6" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">

      <li id="qVF5zktfFHTvZUUxt5CVj" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
        <p>React Grab</p>
        <ul>
          <li id="QJhMHU2S4ZvL3dcUrCVfG" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Element Picker</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="WPm5YrhNpjE6V_siqH8pf" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Copy</p>
                <ul>
                  <li id="BJoGBu1q4kNFzJePGxbWW" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">

                    <ul>

                      </li>
                    </ul>
                  </li>

                      </li>

                        <p/>
                      </li>
                    </ul>
                  </li>
                </ul>
              </li>
            </ul>
          </li>
          <li id="xl1vPq6oPXG3CXcG4BF3P" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
            <p>Visual Edit</p>
            <ul>
              <li id="8iiJ_zQYWDIzri4AWyeZX" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Accept / Reject</p>
                <ul>
                  <li id="-AMqjbgZ_kXjLhVT4EMOA" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                    <p>Accept or reject changes as they appear</p>

                  </li>

                    <p>What happens when you reject?</p>
                  </li>
                </ul>
              </li>
              <li id="0Tt-vO4LuGuqzQVriaeOd" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Should you be able to change the model that is used?</p>
              </li>
              <li id="XK5NWRDf-96Ls7p7REatj" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Is the “.” syntax really that helpful? I’m not sure?</p>
              </li>

                <p>I wonder if, while in progress, it should display the generating … below the prompt itself.</p>
              </li>
              <li id="jAt29DXy6WTmfTVLcZYUL" data-created="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z" data-modified="2025-12-23T09:46:22Z">
                <p>Would this make sense?</p>
